Ohhh Nova Forge is a great name already 🔥
If you’re locking the low-poly aesthetic, here’s a clean, practical breakdown of what else Nova Forge needs implemented to feel complete, intentional, and shippable—not just a tech demo.

I’ll keep this engine-focused, not “AAA fantasy land.”

🎨 Low-Poly Visual Foundation (Core Identity)
If low-poly is the brand, these systems need to exist explicitly, not accidentally:

1. Flat / Controlled Lighting Model
Low-poly breaks if lighting is “too real.”

Implement:

Vertex-color driven shading

Optional unlit / half-lit materials

Hard edge normals (no auto smoothing)

Limited light count per object

Rule: lighting enhances shape, not realism.

2. Material Discipline System
Low-poly engines fall apart when materials sprawl.

You want:

Small fixed material set (10–20 max)

No PBR texture stacks by default

Solid colors + gradients

Palette-driven materials (swap palettes globally)

👉 This lets Nova Forge reskin an entire game in seconds.

🧱 World & Geometry Systems (Very Important)
3. Grid / Chunk World Backbone
Even if the game looks organic, the engine shouldn’t be.

Implement:

World chunks (square or hex)

Deterministic placement

LOD per chunk (not per mesh)

Hard culling distances

This makes:

Farming games

Space scenes

Survival maps
all trivial later.

4. Procedural Shape Builders
This is where Nova Forge earns its name.

Add builders for:

Ships (interior → hull)

Buildings (floor plan → mesh)

Terrain plates

Modular props

All should generate:

Low-poly meshes

Hard edges

Single material where possible

🧍 Characters & Animation (Low-Poly Friendly)
5. Character Rig Standard
You do not want random rigs.

Define:

Fixed bone hierarchy

No facial bones (use shape swaps instead)

Limited animation set

IK only where necessary

Bonus:

Animation retargeting becomes trivial

Modding becomes realistic

6. Silhouette-First Character System
Low-poly lives or dies by silhouette.

Implement:

Body part scaling (torso, limbs, head)

Gear that modifies outline, not detail

Armor as shape layers, not textures

This directly fixes your earlier “stacked blocks” problem.

⚙️ Gameplay Systems Every Engine Needs
7. Data-Driven Everything
No hardcoding gameplay.

You want:

JSON / data tables for items

Stats defined outside code

Behaviors as modules/components

Seed-based randomness

This lets Nova Forge support:

Space games

Farming sims

RPGs

Survival sandboxes
without rewrites.

8. Interaction Layer (Silent Hero)
This is often missing and hurts later.

Implement:

Generic “Interactable” interface

Distance-based prompts

Context-aware actions

No UI logic inside gameplay objects

This keeps UI swappable and clean.

🖥️ Editor & Tooling (This Is Where Indies Win)
9. Custom Authoring UI (No ImGui – locked 👍)
You already made the right call.

You still need:

Shape preview widgets

Procedural seed sliders

Live rebuild buttons

Debug overlays (bounds, chunks, nav)

Think game designer first, not engine dev.

10. Visual Debug Modes
Low-poly engines benefit massively from this.

Add toggles for:

Collision

Chunk borders

LOD levels

AI nav

Interaction zones

These double as teaching tools for contributors.

🧠 AI & Simulation (Keep It Cheap)
11. Simple AI With Personality
Don’t go deep—go readable.

Implement:

State machines (not planners)

Personality modifiers

Deterministic behavior per seed

Low animation count

Low-poly AI should feel intentional, not dumb.

📦 Packaging & Identity
12. Clear “What Nova Forge Is” Definition
This matters more than code.

Your repo should clearly state:

What genres it targets

What it refuses to do

Why low-poly is a feature, not a shortcut

What makes it faster to build games with

This attracts contributors who get it.

🔑 If I Had to Rank What’s Missing Most
Top 5 highest impact additions right now:

Procedural shape builders

Material + palette discipline

Chunked world system

Character silhouette system

Authoring/debug UI

Define a “Low-Poly Ruleset” contributors must follow

Locking scope to shuttle + frigate is the exact right move if you want something that finally looks like a spaceship instead of “procedural geometry soup.”

🛸 Nova Forge: Shuttle & Frigate Generation (Locked Scope)
Class Definitions (Hard Rules)
We do not generate “ships.”
We generate classes with constraints.

Class	Size	Role	Complexity
Shuttle	Small	Transport / Utility	Very Low
Frigate	Medium	Combat / Escort	Medium
No cruisers. No fighters. No stations.
This keeps the math sane.

🧱 Core Principle: Silhouette Before Detail
If the silhouette reads at 20 meters, the ship works.

Everything else is optional.

So Nova Forge ships are built in three layers:

[ Silhouette Frame ]
        ↓
[ Hull Plates ]
        ↓
[ Greebles (minimal, optional) ]
1️⃣ Silhouette Frame Generator (The Most Important System)
This is not mesh-first.
It’s spine-first.

Ship Spine
A ship is defined by a 1D spine:

struct ShipSpineSegment {
    float length;
    float width;
    float height;
    SegmentRole role; // cockpit, cargo, engine, weapon
};
Shuttle Example
[Cockpit]--[Cargo]--[Engine]
Frigate Example
[Cockpit]--[Hab]--[MidHull]--[Reactor]--[EngineBlock]
Each segment:

Scales hull cross-section

Influences hardpoint placement

Controls mass distribution

🔥 This alone stops “stacked blocks” syndrome.

2️⃣ Hull Generation (Low Poly, No Cheating)
Hull Rules
Convex where possible

No bevel spam

No smoothing groups

Hard edges only

Flat shading or vertex color shading

Hull Construction
For each spine segment:

Generate cross-section polygon (hex, octagon, trapezoid)

Extrude to next segment

Weld edges

Auto-cap nose & tail

Allowed cross-sections

Shuttle: rectangle, wedge

Frigate: hex, wide trapezoid

No circles. Ever.
Circles kill low-poly clarity.

3️⃣ Class-Specific Shape Language
🛩 Shuttle Shape Language
Shuttles should feel:

Front-heavy

Short

Functional

Rules:

Cockpit clearly visible

Engines exposed or rear-mounted

Minimal wings or stub fins

Max 5 spine segments

Typical silhouette:

▸■■■■■
🚀 Frigate Shape Language
Frigates should feel:

Long

Layered

Modular

Rules:

Visible mid-hull breakups

Engine block clearly separated

Weapon mounts asymmetrical (optional)

Max 9 spine segments

Typical silhouette:

▸■■■■■■■■■
4️⃣ Engine Block Generator (Iconic Feature)
Engines sell “spaceship” instantly.

Engine Rules
Always rear-facing

Oversized compared to hull

Simple cones, boxes, or hexes

Glow via vertex color, not textures

Engine variants:

Single large thruster (shuttle)

Triple inline (frigate)

Box array (industrial look)

5️⃣ Hardpoints (Minimal but Readable)
No clutter.
Every hardpoint must be visible from silhouette.

Shuttle
Optional top antenna

Optional underside cargo clamp

Zero turrets by default

Frigate
2–4 weapon hardpoints

One dorsal feature (radar, bridge, spine fin)

One ventral detail

Hardpoints are empty sockets by default.
Details snap in later.

6️⃣ Color & Material Discipline
Materials
1 hull color

1 accent color

1 engine glow color

1 detail color (optional)

No textures required.

Palette swap = new faction instantly.

7️⃣ Determinism (Critical)
Given:

{
  "class": "frigate",
  "seed": 4815162342
}
You must always get:

Same spine

Same hull

Same hardpoints

Same colors

This allows:

Ship persistence

NPC identity

Lore consistency

8️⃣ What You Implement FIRST (Order Matters)
Phase 1 – Visual Proof (1–2 weeks)
Spine generator

Hull extrusion

Engine block

Flat shading

If it doesn’t look cool here, stop and tweak.

Phase 2 – Variation (Next)
Cross-section variation

Engine variants

Color palettes

Phase 3 – Gameplay Hooks (Later)
Hardpoint sockets

Interior mapping (future)

Damage zones

🎯 Definition of “Done”
You know this system works when:

10 random seeds → 10 recognizable ships

You can tell shuttle vs frigate instantly

Ships look good without textures

You want to fly one immediately

If you want, next I can:

Sketch the exact spine JSON format

Write pseudo-code for hull extrusion

Design the engine block library

Help you add a ship preview viewport

Or turn one generated frigate into a hero ship

Say the word and we forge 🚀🔥

Oh hell yeah — this is a great spot to level the game up. 🔥
Short answer: yes, absolutely — you can use the models you already uploaded, even if they’re sitting in the project root (though I’ll show you the clean way to do it so it doesn’t turn into asset spaghetti later).

I’ll break this into what to change, how to wire the 3D preview, and how to stop the “stacked blocks” look.

1️⃣ The Core Change: Real 3D Character Preview (Not UI Blocks)

Right now your character preview is conceptually a placeholder — basically a visual stand-in. What you want instead is:

A real 3D actor rendered inside the character creation screen

The Standard UE Way (Clean + Scalable)

You want:

A Character Preview Actor

Rendered through a Scene Capture Component

Displayed inside your UI via a Render Target

This gives you:

Rotation

Zoom

Animations (idle, breathe, stance)

Mesh swapping (race/career gear)

2️⃣ Folder Structure (Yes, You Can Use Root — But Do This)

You can technically use models from the root directory, but I strongly recommend moving them so future-you doesn’t curse present-you 😄

Suggested Structure
Content/
 ├── Characters/
 │   ├── Meshes/
 │   │   ├── SK_Solari_Base.uasset
 │   │   ├── SK_Veyren_Base.uasset
 │   ├── Skeletons/
 │   ├── Animations/
 │   └── Materials/
 ├── UI/
 ├── Blueprints/

👉 If they’re already imported:

You can move assets inside UE safely (right-click → Move)

UE will auto-fix references

3️⃣ Creating the 3D Preview Actor (Key Part)
Step A: Create a Preview Blueprint

Create a Blueprint Actor:

BP_CharacterPreview

Components:

SceneRoot

SkeletalMeshComponent (your character model)

SpringArm

Camera

Optional but recommended:

DirectionalLight

SkyLight

This actor is NOT the player, just a visual mannequin.

Step B: Assign Your Uploaded Models

On the SkeletalMeshComponent:

Assign one of your real character meshes

Assign its skeleton

Set an Idle Animation or Animation Blueprint

💡 This instantly removes the “stacked block” look — that was just a placeholder representation, not a mesh problem.

4️⃣ Rendering the Actor Into the UI (Magic Sauce)
Step A: Scene Capture

Inside BP_CharacterPreview:

Add SceneCaptureComponent2D

Set:

Capture Source: Final Color (LDR)

Texture Target: RT_CharacterPreview

(Create RT_CharacterPreview as a Render Target asset)

Step B: UI Material

Create a Material:

M_CharacterPreview

Settings:

Material Domain: User Interface

Texture Sample → RT_CharacterPreview

Plug into Final Color

Step C: Hook It Into Your Character Creation Widget

In your Widget:

Replace the preview panel with an Image

Assign M_CharacterPreview

Boom 💥
Now your UI is showing a live 3D character

5️⃣ Rotation + Zoom (Like Your UI Text Says)
Rotate

In the Widget:

On Mouse Drag → pass delta to BP_CharacterPreview

Rotate actor on Z (yaw)

Zoom

Mouse Wheel → adjust SpringArm length

Clamp values so it feels nice

This matches your:

“Drag to rotate | Scroll to zoom”
…and actually makes it true 😏

6️⃣ Wiring Race & Career to Real Meshes

Instead of blocks:

Race

Swap Skeletal Mesh

Swap Material Instance

Optional: body proportions (scale bones)

Career

Add / remove:

Armor meshes

Tools

Backpack

Color accents

Example:

Soldier → armor + stance anim
Explorer → lighter gear + relaxed idle
Industrialist → utility gear
Trader → coat + accessories

All without changing the UI logic much.

7️⃣ Important Performance Tip (Don’t Skip This)

Spawn ONE preview actor:

Keep it in a hidden preview level or subscene

Reuse it for all changes

Do NOT respawn per click

This keeps the screen silky smooth.

Ahhhh — got it! 😎 That changes everything. We’re not dealing with UE pipelines at all. This is pure NovaForge custom engine workflow, so everything has to be built from scratch: preview rendering, mesh handling, procedural generation, internal tools, all of it.

Now it makes perfect sense why you were talking about “stacked blocks” — that was a placeholder visual you probably threw in while testing. We can fix it properly in your engine. Let’s break this down specifically for NovaForge’s architecture.

🚀 1️⃣ Character & Ship Preview in NovaForge
You need a live 3D preview system that’s:

Fully engine-native

Works in-editor / debug mode

Supports rotation, zoom, and modular meshes

Components for a Preview System
Preview Camera

Independent camera, not tied to game world

Parameters:

FOV adjustable

Position / rotation controls

Optional orbit mode

Scene Graph Node for Preview Actor

Could be a PreviewActor class

Contains:

MeshNode (skeletal or static)

Optional child nodes for equipment

Transform / rotation controlled by preview UI

Render to Texture / Render Buffer

Draw preview actor into an offscreen framebuffer

Display in UI panel

Engine does this with a normal render pass + custom camera

UI Integration

Texture from render buffer applied to UI panel

Inputs for rotation/zoom translate to actor transform / camera

Result: no “blocks stacked” — real mesh, real lighting, real materials.

🧱 2️⃣ Authoring / Forge Level Concept
Even in a custom engine, the same principle applies:

Hidden “Forge Mode” world / level

Only accessible in editor/debug builds

Hosts preview actors, modular props, ship hull generators

Allows:

Sliders for proportions

Swapping meshes & materials

Live testing of procedural rules

Saving generated configurations as data assets or JSON

This is basically your internal editor + designer sandbox, but fully native.

⚙️ 3️⃣ Procedural Shuttle / Frigate Generation
We can implement a spine + hull + detail system in NovaForge:

Step 1: Define Ship Spine

struct ShipSegment {
    Vec3 dimensions;   // width, height, length
    SegmentRole role;  // cockpit, cargo, reactor, engine
};
struct ShipDefinition {
    std::vector<ShipSegment> spine;
    MaterialSet materials;
};
Step 2: Hull Mesh Generation

For each segment:

Create a cross-section polygon (quad, hex, trapezoid)

Extrude to next segment

Weld vertices, generate normals

Optional: add minimal greebles / fins

Step 3: Engines & Hardpoints

Place engine blocks at rear segment

Place hardpoints at predefined offsets

Materials: base + accent + engine glow

Step 4: Deterministic Seed

Every ship is procedurally generated using a seed

Same seed → same ship

Allows persistence & NPC ships

Step 5: Preview in Forge Mode

Spawn generated ship in hidden level

Attach preview camera + rotation control

Adjust spine / cross-sections with sliders

Save result as JSON / engine data asset

🧰 4️⃣ Recommended Internal Tools for Custom Engine
For NovaForge specifically:

Forge Preview Mode

Characters & ships

Live transform/mesh/material editing

2️⃣ Ship Generator (Shuttle + Frigate)
Purpose: Procedurally generate ships in low-poly style.
Core Pipeline:

Seed & Class Input

Seed = deterministic generation

Class = shuttle or frigate

Spine Definition

List of ShipSegments (cockpit, hull, engine, reactor)

Segment properties: dimensions, role

Hull Generation

Cross-section polygons (quad, trapezoid, hex)

Extrusion along spine

Vertex welding + normal generation

Greebles / Engines / Hardpoints

Engine block placement

Weapon or accessory sockets

Minimal fins/greebles

Material Assignment

Base, accent, engine glow

Preview in Forge Mode

Attach PreviewCamera for orbit/zoom

Slider-based adjustments

Export to Data

Save ship configuration → JSON / Data Asset

Flow:

Seed + Class → Spine → Hull → Details → Materials → Preview → Data Asset
3️⃣ Forge Mode Tools
Purpose: Author & preview all modular content in a safe editor-only environment.
Key Features:

Character Forge

Preview actor sliders: limb lengths, armor bulk, body proportions

Race & career mesh/material swaps

Ship Forge

Adjust spine segment dimensions

Cross-section shape selection

Engine/hardpoint placement

Scene Capture / Render Buffer

Live preview for both characters and ships

Visual Debug Overlays

Bounding volumes

Symmetry planes

Influence zones

Save / Load Controls

Bake settings into JSON or engine-readable data

Flow:

User adjusts sliders → Preview updates → Visual overlay shows bounds → Save → Data Asset
4️⃣ Data Asset Flow
Purpose: Separate authored data from runtime logic for determinism and scalability.

Inputs: Character presets, procedural ship rules, faction / gear definitions

Data Output Types:

JSON (human-readable + mod-friendly)

Engine Data Assets (optimized for runtime)

Runtime Usage:

Character Creation UI reads character assets → spawns preview actor

Game world spawns procedural ships using saved spine + hull + material data

Benefits:

Deterministic generation

Easy modding pipeline

All tuning done in Forge Mode, never hard-coded

Flow Diagram (Simplified):

Forge Tools
   │
   ▼
Adjust / Preview
   │
   ▼
Export → Data Asset / JSON
   │
   ▼
Runtime Systems → Character Spawn / Ship Spawn
🔑 Summary of Workflow
Subsystem	Function	Editor / Runtime Role
Character Preview	Visualize modular characters	Editor: sliders & preview; Runtime: UI display
Ship Generator	Procedural shuttle + frigate	Editor: tweak & bake; Runtime: deterministic spawn
Forge Mode Tools	Author characters, ships, gear	Editor-only safe sandbox
Data Asset Flow	Store & load procedural definitions	Runtime: spawn entities; Editor: save tuned parameters
Big Picture:

Forge Mode = authoring / preview / tuning

Data Asset Flow = deterministic bridge between editor and runtime

Runtime = lightweight, predictable, no heavy editor systems loaded

i want  the game to have an asthetic similar to surroundead art style how do we achieve that  visually?

ChatGPT said:
Ahhh YES — going for a Surrounded-style aesthetic is a brilliant move — that clean, low-poly, colorful, slightly “chunky” style that pops and reads instantly even at small sizes. 🎨✨

Here’s how we can achieve that in NovaForge, fully engine-native, for both characters and ships:

🎨 1️⃣ Core Visual Principles
Low Poly Shapes with Clear Silhouettes

Keep geometry simple.

Limit subdivisions: quads and tris only where needed.

Strong, readable silhouettes matter more than detail.

Flat Shading + Vertex Colors

Avoid PBR or complex textures.

Assign colors per vertex or per mesh face.

Optional: small gradients for accent panels.

Bold, Restricted Color Palettes

3–5 main colors per asset.

Strong contrast between primary shapes.

Example for ships: hull base, accent panel, engine glow, highlight, optional small detail.

Soft Rim / Directional Lighting

One primary light (sun) + ambient fill.

Optional rim light to separate the shape from background.

No heavy shadows or global illumination; keep it flat but readable.

Minimal Textures

Only small patterns or decals for variety.

Most detail comes from shape and color, not textures.

🧱 2️⃣ Character & Ship Implementation
Characters:
Use blocky but organic proportions (slightly exaggerated limbs or head).

Armor and gear = modular shapes layered on top.

Use vertex colors for clothing/armor accents rather than detailed textures.

Keep the number of bones minimal; animation is about readable motion, not subtle detail.

Ships (Shuttle & Frigate):
Use chunked hulls: large, simple sections rather than smooth curves.

Engines = simple cones, cylinders, or trapezoids.

Add color zones per module (cockpit, hull, engine) to give visual variety.

Optional minimal greebles (boxes, panels) for silhouette readability — no micro-detail.

⚡ 3️⃣ Lighting Setup
Even in a custom engine:

Directional Main Light (sunlight)

Hard shadows optional; low-poly style works with simple shadowing.

Ambient / Sky Light

Softens shapes, prevents flat monotone look.

Rim Light (optional)

Single light or shader trick to brighten edges, separates assets from background.

Tip: In low-poly “Surrounded” style, lighting is supportive, not realistic. It’s about readability.

🎨 4️⃣ Material & Color Guidelines
Flat Colors: assign base + accent per mesh

Optional Vertex Gradient: for panels or armor zones

Engine Glow / Highlights: additive color on engines or lights

Contrast Focus: ensure major shapes always pop against the environment

Example palette (frigate ship):

Hull base = dark gray-blue

Cockpit = light gray

Engine glow = cyan

Weapon accents = orange

Small panels = muted purple

🖌 5️⃣ Environment & Background
Keep environment simple, not busy: clean planets, starfields, minimal clutter.

Use gradient skies or simple stars; don’t compete with asset readability.

Optional: subtle fog / ambient tone to give depth without realism.

🛠 Implementation in NovaForge
Mesh Export / Build

Blocky meshes → no smoothing groups

Assign vertex colors per material / face

Renderer / Shader

Flat-shaded shader

Optional rim lighting

Vertex color support

Preview Mode

Enable in Forge Mode to adjust hue/contrast per asset

Test ships + characters under actual lighting conditions

Data Flow

Save palette + material assignment in Data Assets or JSON for deterministic runtime rendering

1️⃣ Character Proportions (Low-Poly Surrounded Style)
Feature	Surrounded Style Guideline
Head	Slightly oversized (1.2–1.5x natural scale) for readability
Torso	Squared-off, blocky; keep silhouette simple
Arms	Slightly thinner than torso, exaggerated joints optional
Legs	Slightly longer than torso for dynamic posture
Hands / Feet	Minimal geometry; suggest simple block shapes
Armor / Gear	Modular, chunky plates; layered over base mesh
Overall	Exaggerate shapes for readability, not realism
Tip: Even a low-poly character with only ~200–400 tris can read clearly if proportions are strong.

2️⃣ Ship Silhouettes (Shuttle & Frigate)
Shuttle
Length: 1.5–2x width

Hull: wedge or rectangular prism

Cockpit: front protrusion

Engines: rear cylinders / cones

Fins / Wings: optional, minimal

Silhouette: compact and front-heavy

Frigate
Length: 3–4x width

Hull: modular segments (cockpit → mid → reactor → engines)

Engine blocks: multiple cones or cylinders

Weapon hardpoints: minimal, placed along spine

Greebles / Panels: sparse, to suggest complexity without clutter

Silhouette: long, modular, instantly readable

Station (Surrounded Style)
Cubic modules + pipes

Large docking bays readable at distance

Minimal details: large blocks, ramps, antennas

Color zones define function (engineering vs habitation vs hangar)

Asteroids
Blocky, faceted geometry

Irregular shapes with 3–6 main facets

Small accent cracks or vertex color variations

Low-poly: 50–300 tris per rock depending on scale

3️⃣ Color Palette & Shading Rules
Palette
Asset	Base	Accent	Highlight	Optional
Characters	Neutral gray / earth tones	Armor color	Light highlight	Face / hair
Ships	Dark gray / navy	Cockpit / panel	Engine glow	Weapon / small panels
Stations	Muted gray / brown	Doors / docking	Window glow	Antennas / lights
Asteroids	Dark gray / stone	Rock cracks / mineral	None	N/A
Shading
Flat Shading: no gradients by default

Vertex Colors: for panels, zones, or accent areas

Rim Lighting: subtle to separate assets from background

No complex textures: Surrounded style relies on color + shape

4️⃣ Example “Good vs Bad” Low-Poly Styling
Type	Good	Bad
Character	Clear head + torso silhouette, readable limbs, modular armor	Tiny head, same width for arms/legs, too many tiny details
Ship	Long / wedge silhouette, blocky hull, engine/weapon accents readable	Round blended hull, micro greebles, silhouette messy
Station	Distinct modules, large docking bays, color zones	Random geometry, tiny modules, no readable function
Asteroids	Blocky irregular shape, visible facets, color contrast	Smooth spheres, small polygons, no variation
5️⃣ Implementation in NovaForge
Characters:

Base mesh = low-poly skeleton (~200–400 tris)

Armor / gear = modular blocks

Vertex color zones = base + accent + highlight

Ships:

Hull generation = spine + extrusion + simple cross-section

Engine & greebles = minimal cubes / cones

Color zones per hull module

Stations / Asteroids:

Stations = cubes + ramps + minimal pipes

Asteroids = faceted blocks, random vertex color variations

Low-poly meshes, easy to spawn procedurally

Lighting:

Single directional light + ambient fill

Optional rim lighting to separate shapes

Shadows minimal or baked if needed

You can pull real visual inspiration from industrial mining ships like those from EVE Online — heavy, functional, modular, purpose‑driven designs that read instantly as “industrial miner” rather than sleek combat craft.

Here’s how to formally tie interior function → modular exterior generation:

🎯 1️⃣ Module‑Driven Exterior Generation
🧠 Concept: Systems Weight → Appearance
Your ship generator already has modules for interiors. Let each interior system contribute a “weight” to exterior design:

Interior System	Exterior Impact
Mining systems	Mining booms, industrial trusses, cargo pods
Cargo capacity	Bulk storage modules, extended holds
Refinery systems	Conveyor housings, visible vents, heat radiators
Power generation	Engine housings, reactors with heat sinks

This means ships are never arbitrary collections of shapes — exterior modules are driven by functional needs.

Functional Blocks

Mining arrays

Refinery units

Cargo pods

Engine clusters

Connectors

Trusses

Support struts

Utility conduits

📐 4️⃣ Exterior Generation Pipeline (Step‑by‑Step)
Here’s a concrete pipeline for your procedural generator:

🔹 Input
{
  "seed": 12345678,
  "classification": "industrial",
  "systems": {
    "mining": 0.8,
    "refinery": 0.5,
    "cargo": 0.7,
    "support": 0.4
  }
}
🔹 Processing
Assign segments

Reactor → core block

Mining weight → mining boom modules

Cargo → storage blocks

Systems combine to decide how many of each module

Select module variations

Predefined library per function (mining boom types, cargo pod sizes)

Weighted by system strength

Snap modules to spine

Place core modules center

Place functional modules asymmetrically for interest

Add connectors & struts between blocks

Assign Colors

Industrial palette driven by function

Mining → yellow/gray

Refinery → dark gray/steel

Support → accent colors

Finalize Silhouette

Ensure silhouette reads clearly at distance

Pop against background

⚙ Refinery‑Heavy
Large chimney/vent stacks

Ramp Node	Connects bay floor to exterior hull	Drives ramp mesh size and placement
Elevator Node	Connects bay to ship interior decks	Procedural placement near center-of-mass
Node Placement Rules:

Always near ship center-of-mass for balance.

Docking nodes are evenly spaced inside bay width.

Upgrade panel always faces docking nodes; player can interact from any valid tile.

Ramp node placed at bay exit; automatically scales to bay width.

🪐 2️⃣ Grav Bike Slot with Solar/Battery Module
Slot Components:

Slot Anchor: Procedural point for grav bike placement.

Battery Module: Upgradable stats; visually a small block on bike.

Solar Attachment: Optional attachment for passive charging.

Slot Constraints: Cannot overlap rover slots; placed along bay edge for easy exterior ramp access.

Behavior Rules:

Solar module influences charging mechanics while docked or in open space.

Upgrades update vehicle stats and low-poly visual representation (small panel, battery cube, or solar panel).

Grav bike dock is smaller than rover docking nodes; visually compact but readable.

🔧 3️⃣ Upgrade Panel Logic
Panel Features:

Interactable UI Node: Procedural in interior layout; faces docking nodes.

Vehicle Selection: Shows docked vehicles (rover, grav bike).

Module Selection: Swap or upgrade modules (battery, drill, cargo, solar).

Preview Functionality: Live preview of changes in low-poly style (modular blocks change color/size).

Save Changes: Updates vehicle configuration in engine data assets; affects runtime stats.

Procedural Placement Rules:

One panel per bay or per docking cluster.

Panel location scales with bay width: can split into multiple nodes if multiple vehicles.

Panel orientation always faces player access path.

🏗 4️⃣ Ramp + Hull Integration
Ramp Design:

Placement: Automatically at bay exit node.

Scaling: Width = bay width + padding; length scales to reach space hull clearance.

Animation: Opens / lowers when bay accessed; retracts when closed.

Exterior Hull Implications:

Hull meshes are modular and snapped to interior bay nodes.

Bay underside shows bulge proportional to bay width and vehicle count.

Ramp door and hatch panels are separate low-poly meshes; optionally animate hinges or sliding panels.

Low-Poly Surrounded-Style Considerations:

Flat-shaded meshes, minimal triangles.

Vertex color differentiation for bay vs hull.

Functional trusses or struts for industrial look (especially mining-oriented ships).

Clear silhouette: hull bulge, ramp, and docking points readable from distance.

🌌 5️⃣ Exterior Hull Representation Rules
Hull blocks snap around interior bay modules.

Mining/Industrial Weighting: Add functional greebles, piping, or engine/exhaust units near bay if ship is mining-heavy.

Visual Cues for Vehicle Functionality:

Bay doors / ramps → indicate access

Minor vent panels or small hull protrusions → indicate docking / repair activity

Color & Material:

Hull base = dark gray

Bay/ramp = industrial yellow/gray

Panels / functional highlights = orange / muted accent

Hull geometry extrudes to match bay width.

Ahhh, now we’re getting into true procedural generation territory — you don’t want a static image, you want code to generate that modular rover bay, ramp, docking slots, and exterior hull in your engine dynamically. Let’s break this down into a concrete, data-driven procedural system that NovaForge can implement without any pre-baked art. 🚀

1️⃣ Core Idea
Everything in that infographic can be represented as modular nodes + mesh templates:

Modules = pieces of ship (floor tiles, docking platforms, ramps, walls, hull blocks).

Nodes = connection points that define snapping, placement, and hierarchy.

Rules / Weights = logic to decide what modules go where based on interior systems (mining, cargo, exploration).

Procedural Hull Extrusion = exterior hull meshes are generated from the footprint of interior nodes.

This is all math and data, no hand-crafted art needed.

2️⃣ Data Structures
Example C++/pseudo-code structure:

struct Module {
    string type;             // "floor", "dock", "ramp", "panel", "hull"
    Vector3 size;            // width, height, depth
    Vector3 localOffset;     // relative to parent node
    vector<Node> attachPoints; // points where other modules snap
    Color color;             // low-poly color for Surrounded style
};

struct Node {
    Vector3 position;
    Quaternion rotation;
    string type;             // "docking", "panel", "ramp", "elevator"
    Module* attachedModule;  // module occupying this node
};

struct RoverBay {
    Node elevatorNode;
    Node rampNode;
    vector<Node> roverDockNodes;
    Node gravBikeNode;
    vector<Node> upgradePanelNodes;
};
Key idea: Each module is a simple box/plane/low-poly block. The nodes define how they snap together and orient.

3️⃣ Generation Steps (Algorithm)
Define Bay Layout

RoverBay bay;
bay.elevatorNode.position = ship.CoM;
bay.rampNode.position = bay.elevatorNode.position - Vector3(0, 0, bayLength/2);
bay.roverDockNodes = GenerateRoverNodes(bayWidth, numberOfRovers);
bay.gravBikeNode = GenerateGravBikeNode(bayWidth);
bay.upgradePanelNodes = GeneratePanelNodes(bayWidth);
Snap Modules

for (Node& node : bay.allNodes()) {
    node.attachedModule = CreateModuleForNode(node.type);
    node.attachedModule->localOffset = node.position;
}
Generate Hull from Footprint

HullMesh = ExtrudeHullFromNodes(bay.allNodes());
ApplyIndustrialDetails(HullMesh, miningWeight, cargoWeight);
ExtrudeHullFromNodes:

Use the 2D footprint of bay + ramps.

Extrude outward/upward to create hull blocks.

Add trusses or pipes procedurally based on weight of systems.

Assign Colors & Low-Poly Style

for (Module& m : allModules) {
    m.color = ChooseColorBySystemWeight(ship.systems);
    // Flat shading, no textures needed
}
Deploy Vehicles

Docked vehicles use dockNode.position + dockNode.rotation.

Modules on vehicles (battery, solar panels) are procedural cubes attached to vehicle root.

4️⃣ Procedural Ramp + Animation
Ramp is just a simple rectangular module.

Animated by rotating / translating along a hinge axis:

ramp.rotation = Lerp(closedRotation, openRotation, animationAlpha);
ramp.position = Lerp(closedPosition, openPosition, animationAlpha);
Hull bulge around ramp is generated by scaling hull blocks to match ramp width/height.

5️⃣ Vehicle Upgrade Modules
Each vehicle has module slots (battery, drill, solar).

Modules are simple cubes/primitives that attach at predefined positions.

Stats updated in data; visuals automatically match module size/color.

6️⃣ Industrial Cues for Low-Poly Exterior
Procedural decorations:

Pipes = cylinders connecting hull blocks

Trusses = flat elongated boxes

Panels = colored quads

Placement rules based on system weights: mining-heavy ships get more external machinery nodes.

Everything in your infographic is nodes + simple low-poly primitives + procedural rules:

Infographic Element	Procedural Equivalent

Upgrade Panels	Panel node + slot array

NovaForge Procedural Ship Generator — High-Level Pseudo-Code
// Input structure
struct ShipConfig {
    string shipClass;            // e.g., "Frigate", "Shuttle"
    float miningWeight;          // 0..1
    float cargoWeight;           // 0..1
    float combatWeight;          // 0..1
    float explorationWeight;     // 0..1
    int seed;                    // deterministic generation
};

// Node definition
struct Node {
    Vector3 position;
    Quaternion rotation;
    string type;                 // "docking", "panel", "ramp", "elevator", etc.
};

// Module definition
struct Module {
    string type;                 // "floor", "dock", "ramp", "panel", "hull", etc.
    Vector3 size;
    Color color;
    Node* parentNode;
};

// Vehicle module slot
struct VehicleModule {
    string type;                 // e.g., "battery", "solar", "drill"
    Vector3 localOffset;
    Color color;
};
Step 1 — Generate Rover Bay Nodes
RoverBayNodes GenerateRoverBayNodes(ShipConfig config) {
    RoverBayNodes bay;

    // Determine bay size based on ship class & exploration weight
    float bayWidth = Lerp(4.0f, 12.0f, config.explorationWeight);
    float bayLength = Lerp(6.0f, 18.0f, config.explorationWeight);

    // Center elevator node at ship CoM
    bay.elevatorNode = Node(Vector3(0,0,0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1), "elevator");

    // Ramp node at bay front
    bay.rampNode = Node(Vector3(0, -bayLength/2, 0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1), "ramp");

    // Rover docking nodes (1-3 depending on bay size)
    int roverSlots = (bayWidth > 8.0f) ? 3 : 2;
    for(int i=0; i<roverSlots; i++) {
        float xOffset = -bayWidth/2 + (i+0.5f)*(bayWidth/roverSlots);
        bay.roverDockNodes.push_back(Node(Vector3(xOffset, 0, 0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1), "roverDock"));
    }

    // Grav bike slot if exploration weight > 0.5
    if(config.explorationWeight > 0.5f) {
        bay.gravBikeNode = Node(Vector3(bayWidth/2 + 1, 0, 0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1), "gravBikeDock");
    }

    // Upgrade panels
    bay.upgradePanelNodes.push_back(Node(Vector3(-bayWidth/2 - 1, 1, 0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1), "panel"));

    return bay;
}
Step 2 — Snap Modules to Nodes
vector<Module> SnapModules(RoverBayNodes bay) {
    vector<Module> modules;

    // Elevator
    modules.push_back(Module("elevator", Vector3(1,1,2), Color::Gray(), &bay.elevatorNode));

    // Ramp
    modules.push_back(Module("ramp", Vector3(bay.rampNode.position.x*2, 1, 3), Color::Yellow(), &bay.rampNode));

    // Rover docks
    for(Node dock : bay.roverDockNodes) {
        modules.push_back(Module("floorDock", Vector3(2,1,2), Color::Gray(), &dock));
    }

    // Grav bike
    if(bay.gravBikeNode.type != "") {
        modules.push_back(Module("floorDock", Vector3(1.5f,1,2), Color::Orange(), &bay.gravBikeNode));
    }

    // Upgrade panels
    for(Node panel : bay.upgradePanelNodes) {
        modules.push_back(Module("panel", Vector3(1,2,0.5f), Color::Blue(), &panel));
    }

    return modules;
}
Step 3 — Procedural Hull Extrusion
Mesh BuildExteriorHull(vector<Module> interiorModules, ShipConfig config) {
    Mesh hull;

    // Determine hull footprint from modules
    float hullWidth = MaxX(interiorModules) - MinX(interiorModules) + 2;
    float hullLength = MaxY(interiorModules) - MinY(interiorModules) + 4;
    float hullHeight = Lerp(4.0f, 10.0f, config.cargoWeight);

    // Hull main block
    hull.AddBox(Vector3(0,0,hullHeight/2), Vector3(hullWidth, hullLength, hullHeight), Color::DarkGray());

    // Industrial cues based on mining weight
    int trussCount = int(config.miningWeight * 5);
    for(int i=0; i<trussCount; i++) {
        float x = RandomRange(-hullWidth/2, hullWidth/2);
        float y = RandomRange(-hullLength/2, hullLength/2);
        hull.AddBox(Vector3(x,y,hullHeight/2), Vector3(0.2f, hullLength/8, hullHeight/2), Color::Gray());
    }

    // Add hull extrusions for ramp and bay
    hull.AddBox(Vector3(0, -hullLength/2 - 1, hullHeight/4), Vector3(hullWidth, 2, hullHeight/2), Color::Yellow());

    return hull;
}
Step 4 — Assign Vehicle Upgrade Modules
void AssignVehicleModules(Module& vehicleModule, ShipConfig config) {
    vehicleModule.AddChild(VehicleModule("battery", Vector3(0,0,0.5f), Color::Orange()));
    if(config.explorationWeight > 0.5f) {
        vehicleModule.AddChild(VehicleModule("solarPanel", Vector3(0,0,1.0f), Color::Yellow()));
    }
}
✅ Step 5 — Summary Flow
Input: ShipConfig (class + system weights + seed)

Generate Interior Nodes: GenerateRoverBayNodes(config)

Snap Modules to Nodes: SnapModules(bay)

Build Exterior Hull: BuildExteriorHull(modules, config)

Assign Vehicle Modules: AssignVehicleModules()

Render / Spawn in Engine:

All modules are low-poly cubes/primitives

Exterior hull reflects bay footprint

Industrial cues added based on mining/cargo weighting

This produces:

Procedural belly rover bay

Docking slots (rover + grav bike)

Upgrade panel

Ramp + hull integration

Exterior Surrounded-style hull with industrial cues

ChatGPT said:
Ahhh, got it — I totally understand now. We are staying in pure code / data / procedural generation logic, no images, no art, nothing rendered visually unless you explicitly ask for it. 😅

Rover bay interior nodes

NovaForge Procedural Ship Generator — Text & Data Only
// ----------------------------
// INPUT CONFIGURATION
// ----------------------------
struct ShipConfig {
    string shipClass;            // "Frigate", "Shuttle", etc.
    float miningWeight;          // 0..1
    float cargoWeight;           // 0..1
    float explorationWeight;     // 0..1
    float combatWeight;          // 0..1
    int seed;                    // deterministic
};

// ----------------------------
// NODE DEFINITIONS
// ----------------------------
struct Node {
    string type;                 // "elevator", "ramp", "roverDock", "gravBikeDock", "upgradePanel"
    Vector3 position;            // relative to ship CoM
    Quaternion rotation;         // orientation
};

struct Module {
    string type;                 // "floor", "panel", "ramp", "hull"
    Vector3 size;                // width, length, height
    Node* parentNode;            // which node it attaches to
    Color color;                 // low-poly flat color
};

struct VehicleModule {
    string type;                 // "battery", "solarPanel", "drill", "cargoPod"
    Vector3 localOffset;         // relative to vehicle
    Color color;
};

// ----------------------------
// STEP 1: GENERATE ROVER BAY NODES
// ----------------------------
RoverBayNodes GenerateRoverBayNodes(ShipConfig config) {
    RoverBayNodes bay;
    
    // Elevator node at center of mass
    bay.elevatorNode = Node("elevator", Vector3(0,0,0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1));
    
    // Ramp at front of bay
    float bayLength = 6.0f + config.explorationWeight * 12.0f; // scales by exploration
    bay.rampNode = Node("ramp", Vector3(0, -bayLength/2, 0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1));
    
    // Rover docking nodes
    int roverSlots = (config.explorationWeight > 0.5f) ? 3 : 2;
    float bayWidth = 4.0f + config.explorationWeight * 8.0f;
    for(int i=0;i<roverSlots;i++){
        float x = -bayWidth/2 + (i + 0.5f) * (bayWidth / roverSlots);
        bay.roverDockNodes.push_back(Node("roverDock", Vector3(x,0,0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1)));
    }
    
    // Grav bike slot if exploration-heavy
    if(config.explorationWeight > 0.5f){
        bay.gravBikeNode = Node("gravBikeDock", Vector3(bayWidth/2 + 1, 0, 0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1));
    }
    
    // Upgrade panel nodes
    bay.upgradePanelNodes.push_back(Node("upgradePanel", Vector3(-bayWidth/2 - 1,1,0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1)));
    
    return bay;
}

// ----------------------------
// STEP 2: SNAP MODULES TO NODES
// ----------------------------
vector<Module> SnapModules(RoverBayNodes bay) {
    vector<Module> modules;

    modules.push_back(Module("elevator", Vector3(1,1,2), &bay.elevatorNode, Color::Gray()));
    modules.push_back(Module("ramp", Vector3( bay.rampNode.position.x*2, 1, 3 ), &bay.rampNode, Color::Yellow()));

    for(Node dock : bay.roverDockNodes){
        modules.push_back(Module("floorDock", Vector3(2,1,2), &dock, Color::Gray()));
    }

    if(bay.gravBikeNode.type != ""){
        modules.push_back(Module("floorDock", Vector3(1.5f,1,2), &bay.gravBikeNode, Color::Orange()));
    }

    for(Node panel : bay.upgradePanelNodes){
        modules.push_back(Module("panel", Vector3(1,2,0.5f), &panel, Color::Blue()));
    }

    return modules;
}

// ----------------------------
// STEP 3: BUILD EXTERIOR HULL
// ----------------------------
Mesh BuildExteriorHull(vector<Module> interiorModules, ShipConfig config) {
    Mesh hull;

    // Compute footprint from interior modules
    float hullWidth = MaxX(interiorModules) - MinX(interiorModules) + 2;
    float hullLength = MaxY(interiorModules) - MinY(interiorModules) + 4;
    float hullHeight = 4.0f + config.cargoWeight * 6.0f;

    hull.AddBox(Vector3(0,0,hullHeight/2), Vector3(hullWidth, hullLength, hullHeight), Color::DarkGray());

    // Industrial cues for mining
    int trussCount = int(config.miningWeight * 5);
    for(int i=0;i<trussCount;i++){
        float x = RandomRange(-hullWidth/2, hullWidth/2);
        float y = RandomRange(-hullLength/2, hullLength/2);
        hull.AddBox(Vector3(x,y,hullHeight/2), Vector3(0.2f, hullLength/8, hullHeight/2), Color::Gray());
    }

    // Hull extrusion for ramp and bay
    hull.AddBox(Vector3(0, -hullLength/2 - 1, hullHeight/4), Vector3(hullWidth, 2, hullHeight/2), Color::Yellow());

    return hull;
}

// ----------------------------
// STEP 4: ASSIGN VEHICLE MODULES
// ----------------------------
void AssignVehicleModules(Module& vehicle, ShipConfig config) {
    vehicle.AddChild(VehicleModule("battery", Vector3(0,0,0.5f), Color::Orange()));
    if(config.explorationWeight > 0.5f){
        vehicle.AddChild(VehicleModule("solarPanel", Vector3(0,0,1.0f), Color::Yellow()));
    }
}

// ----------------------------
// STEP 5: GENERATION PIPELINE
// ----------------------------
Ship GenerateShip(ShipConfig config){
    RoverBayNodes bay = GenerateRoverBayNodes(config);
    vector<Module> interiorModules = SnapModules(bay);
    Mesh hull = BuildExteriorHull(interiorModules, config);

    // Attach vehicle modules to docks
    for(Module& m : interiorModules){
        if(m.type == "floorDock"){
            AssignVehicleModules(m, config);
        }
    }

    Ship ship;
    ship.interiorModules = interiorModules;
    ship.hull = hull;

    return ship;
}
✅ Key Notes
Everything is deterministic: same seed → same ship.

Low-poly aesthetic is enforced via primitives + flat colors.

Ramp, docking, panels all snap to procedural nodes.

Hull is extruded from interior footprint — no pre-made art.

Vehicle modules (battery, solar) are procedural attachments.

Industrial styling: optional trusses / pipes scaled by system weights.

ChatGPT said:
Exactly — let’s take it to the next level. 🚀

Here’s how we can extend your procedural generator to multi-deck ships, fully driven by interior systems, with no art needed, purely code/data-driven, while preserving that low-poly Surrounded-style look:

Fully Procedural Multi-Deck Ship Generator
1️⃣ Conceptual Overview
Each deck has its own node grid: elevator, ramps, docking, panels.

System weights (mining, cargo, exploration, combat) influence:

Deck count

Deck footprint (width/length/height)

Module types per deck (industrial trusses, storage pods, weapon mounts)

Hull extrusion aggregates all decks into a single cohesive exterior.

Vehicle bays (rovers, grav bikes) are always on specific decks, usually central or lowest.

2️⃣ Data Structures
struct Deck {
    string name;                 // "Belly", "Cargo", "Bridge", etc.
    Vector3 offsetFromCoM;       // relative vertical offset
    vector<Node> nodes;          // procedural interior nodes
    vector<Module> modules;      // snapped modules
};

struct Ship {
    ShipConfig config;
    vector<Deck> decks;
    Mesh hull;                    // exterior hull built from all decks
};
3️⃣ Deck Node Generation (Procedural)
Deck GenerateDeck(string name, Vector3 offset, ShipConfig config){
    Deck deck;
    deck.name = name;
    deck.offsetFromCoM = offset;

    // Elevator node connects decks vertically
    deck.nodes.push_back(Node("elevator", Vector3(0,0,0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1)));

    // Ramp node if this deck has external access (e.g., belly bay)
    if(name == "Belly"){
        float bayLength = 6.0f + config.explorationWeight*12.0f;
        deck.nodes.push_back(Node("ramp", Vector3(0,-bayLength/2,0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1)));
    }

    // Rover docking nodes
    if(name == "Belly"){
        int roverSlots = (config.explorationWeight > 0.5f) ? 3 : 2;
        float bayWidth = 4.0f + config.explorationWeight*8.0f;
        for(int i=0;i<roverSlots;i++){
            float x = -bayWidth/2 + (i+0.5f)*(bayWidth/roverSlots);
            deck.nodes.push_back(Node("roverDock", Vector3(x,0,0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1)));
        }
        // Grav bike
        if(config.explorationWeight > 0.5f)
            deck.nodes.push_back(Node("gravBikeDock", Vector3(bayWidth/2+1,0,0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1)));
        // Upgrade panel
        deck.nodes.push_back(Node("upgradePanel", Vector3(-bayWidth/2-1,1,0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1)));
    }

    // Additional nodes based on system weight
    if(config.miningWeight > 0.3f) deck.nodes.push_back(Node("miningStation", Vector3(1,1,0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1)));
    if(config.cargoWeight > 0.3f) deck.nodes.push_back(Node("cargoBay", Vector3(-1,1,0), Quaternion(0,0,0,1)));

    return deck;
}
4️⃣ Snap Modules Per Deck
void SnapDeckModules(Deck& deck){
    for(Node& node : deck.nodes){
        if(node.type == "ramp") deck.modules.push_back(Module("ramp", Vector3(3,6,1), &node, Color::Yellow()));
        else if(node.type == "elevator") deck.modules.push_back(Module("elevator", Vector3(1,1,2), &node, Color::Gray()));
        else if(node.type == "roverDock" || node.type == "gravBikeDock") deck.modules.push_back(Module("floorDock", Vector3(2,1,2), &node, Color::Gray()));
        else if(node.type == "upgradePanel") deck.modules.push_back(Module("panel", Vector3(1,2,0.5f), &node, Color::Blue()));
        else if(node.type == "miningStation") deck.modules.push_back(Module("miningModule", Vector3(2,2,2), &node, Color::Orange()));
        else if(node.type == "cargoBay") deck.modules.push_back(Module("cargoModule", Vector3(3,3,2), &node, Color::Brown()));
    }
}
5️⃣ Procedural Multi-Deck Hull Generation
Mesh BuildMultiDeckHull(vector<Deck> decks, ShipConfig config){
    Mesh hull;

    for(Deck& deck : decks){
        // Hull footprint from deck modules
        float width = MaxX(deck.modules)-MinX(deck.modules)+2;
        float length = MaxY(deck.modules)-MinY(deck.modules)+2;
        float height = 2.0f + config.cargoWeight*4.0f; // deck height scaled by cargo

        Vector3 deckOffset = deck.offsetFromCoM + Vector3(0,0,height/2);
        hull.AddBox(deckOffset, Vector3(width,length,height), Color::DarkGray());

        // Add industrial cues per deck based on mining/cargo weight
        int trusses = int(config.miningWeight*3);
        for(int i=0;i<trusses;i++){
            float x = RandomRange(-width/2,width/2);
            float y = RandomRange(-length/2,length/2);
            hull.AddBox(deckOffset + Vector3(x,y,height/2), Vector3(0.2,length/8,height/2), Color::Gray());
        }
    }

    return hull;
}
6️⃣ Full Ship Generation Pipeline
Ship GenerateMultiDeckShip(ShipConfig config){
    Ship ship;
    ship.config = config;

    // Generate decks
    vector<string> deckNames = {"Belly","Cargo","Bridge"};
    float verticalOffset = 0;
    for(string name : deckNames){
        Deck deck = GenerateDeck(name, Vector3(0,0,verticalOffset), config);
        SnapDeckModules(deck);
        ship.decks.push_back(deck);
        verticalOffset += 3 + config.cargoWeight*2; // stack decks vertically
    }

    // Build exterior hull
    ship.hull = BuildMultiDeckHull(ship.decks, config);

    // Assign vehicle modules for docking nodes
    for(Deck& deck : ship.decks){
        for(Module& m : deck.modules){
            if(m.type == "floorDock") AssignVehicleModules(m, config);
        }
    }

    return ship;
}

Decks stacked vertically → interior system layout dictates hull shape.

Procedural nodes per deck → docks, ramps, panels, cargo, mining modules.

Exterior hull automatically extrudes from all decks → Surrounded-style low-poly aesthetic.

Vehicle modules attach automatically at docking nodes.

Industrial cues (trusses, pipes) dynamically added per system weight.

Fully deterministic via seed.

void TryAttachModule(ShipNode& baseNode, ModuleDefinition& newModule)
{
    for (auto& socket : baseNode.sockets)
    {
        if (socket.isFree)
        {
            Vector3 attachPosition =
                baseNode.position +
                (socket.direction * baseNode.bounds);

            if (!CheckCollision(attachPosition, newModule.bounds))
            {
                SpawnModuleAt(attachPosition);
                break;
            }
        }
    }
}

Vector3 ComputeCenterOfMass()
{
    float totalMass = 0;
    Vector3 weightedPos = Vector3(0,0,0);

    for (auto& node : shipNodes)
    {
        totalMass += node.mass;
        weightedPos += node.position * node.mass;
    }

    return weightedPos / totalMass;
}
Rover bay placed closest to this point.

Recursive Expansion Function
void ExpandDeck(DeckNode& node)
{
    if (node.expansionBudget <= 0)
        return;

    for (auto& socket : node.sockets)
    {
        if (ShouldExpand(socket))
        {
            Module newModule = GenerateModuleForRole();
            
            AttachModule(node, newModule);

            DeckNode child = ConvertToDeckNode(newModule);
            child.expansionBudget = node.expansionBudget * 0.6f;

            ExpandDeck(child);
        }
    }
}
Expansion Control Rules
Prevent infinite madness:

Depth cap by ship class

Budget shrinks per generation

Mining weight increases side probability

Combat weight increases forward probability

Direction Bias Based on Role
float sideBias   = miningWeight * 0.7f;
float forwardBias = combatWeight * 0.8f;
float rearBias   = engineWeight * 0.9f;

3️⃣ Combat Damage Deformation System
(Damage reshapes hull dynamically)

Not just HP bars.

We deform geometry procedurally.

Damage Model
Each hull module stores:

struct DamageState
{
    float integrity;        // 0..1
    float deformationLevel; // how warped it is
    bool structuralFailure;
};
On Impact
void ApplyDamage(Module& module, float force)
{
    module.integrity -= force;

    if (module.integrity < 0.5f)
        module.deformationLevel += force * 0.3f;

    if (module.integrity <= 0)
        module.structuralFailure = true;
}
Deformation Pass
void DeformModule(Module& module)
{
    for (auto& vertex : module.mesh.vertices)
    {
        vertex.position += 
            RandomVector() * module.deformationLevel * 0.2f;
    }
}
Structural Collapse Chain
If structural module fails:

if (module.isStructuralCore && module.structuralFailure)
    TriggerStressRecalculation();
Branches can snap off.

You now have:

Hull tearing

Asymmetrical battle damage

Industrial beams exposed

Functional performance degradation

damage deformation is natural.

struct HangarModule

2️⃣ Ship Build Validation in Hangar
Before a ship starts building:

bool CanManufactureShip(HangarModule& hangar, Ship& ship)
{
    if (ship.totalSize > hangar.maxManufactureSize)
        return false;

    for (auto& cls : ship.classes)
        if (std::find(hangar.allowedClasses.begin(), hangar.allowedClasses.end(), cls) == hangar.allowedClasses.end())
            return false;

    return HasRequiredMaterials(hangar, ship);
}
This allows multi-module hangars to stack capabilities, e.g., a medium dock can build Frigates but not Cruisers.

Large “all-in” modules can produce any class.

void ManufactureShip(HangarModule& hangar, ShipBlueprint& blueprint)
{
    if (!CanManufactureShip(hangar, blueprint.ship))
        return;

    blueprint.ship.seed = GenerateSeed(); // deterministic
    blueprint.ship.locked = true;

    float buildTime = blueprint.ship.complexityScore / hangar.buildSpeedMultiplier;
    StartBuildTimer(hangar, blueprint, buildTime);
}
Once StartBuildTimer completes → ship moves to main hangar or deployment bay.

2️⃣ Drone Build Validation
bool CanManufactureDrone(FabBay& bay, Drone& drone)
{
    if (drone.size > bay.maxManufactureSize)
        return false;

    if (std::find(bay.supportedDrones.begin(), bay.supportedDrones.end(), drone.type) == bay.supportedDrones.end())
        return false;

    return HasRequiredResources(bay, drone);
}
Bay size constrains drone scale

Type constrains functionality (a small fab bay may not support heavy attack drones)

3️⃣ Drone On-Demand Queue
Each ship has a drone dock with slots:

struct DroneSlot
{
    Drone drone;
    bool active;
    bool docked;
};
Fab bay creates drones on-demand:

void RequestDrone(FabBay& bay, Drone& drone, Ship& host)
{
    if (!CanManufactureDrone(bay, drone))
        return;

    drone.buildTime = baseDroneBuildTime * drone.buildTimeMultiplier / bay.buildSpeedMultiplier;
    StartBuildTimer(bay, drone, drone.buildTime);

    // Once done
    DockDroneToHost(host, drone);
}
Build time respects fab bay size + drone complexity

Drones are seed-locked → deterministic procedural outcome

4️⃣ Drone Capabilities Driven by Host Ship
Drone features depend on host ship’s installed systems and modules:

Weapons → drones get attack modules

Shield generators → drones get defensive upgrades

Mining tools → drones can act as support salvage/mining units

Sensor suites → drones gain scouting/hacking capabilities

void AssignDroneModules(Drone& drone, Ship& host)
{
    for (auto& module : host.installedModules)
    {
        if (module.type == ModuleType::WeaponControl)
            drone.modulesInstalled.push_back(GenerateAttackModule());
        else if (module.type == ModuleType::ShieldGenerator)
            drone.modulesInstalled.push_back(GenerateDefenseModule());
        else if (module.type == ModuleType::UtilityNode)
            drone.modulesInstalled.push_back(GenerateSupportModule());
    }
}
Ensures drones scale organically with ship capability

No art needed; purely procedural

5️⃣ Docking & Energy Management
Drone slots must account for:

Docking physical space (procedural node attachment)

Energy allocation from host ship: each drone draws power

float AllocateDroneEnergy(Ship& host, Drone& drone)
{
    float availableEnergy = host.energyCapacity - host.activeEnergyDraw;
    drone.energySupply = std::min(drone.energyRequirement, availableEnergy);
    host.activeEnergyDraw += drone.energySupply;
}
Drones become inactive if host power is insufficient

Adds strategic layer to ship and fab design

void ManufactureOrUpgradeVehicle(BellyBay& bay, Vehicle& vehicle)
{

        return;

    {

        {
            InstallModule(vehicle, module);
            ConsumeResources(bay, module);
        }
    }

    DockVehicle(bay, vehicle); // store vehicle in slot
}

1️⃣ Core Procedural Production System
At the top level, everything is driven by a Production Node Graph, where every “buildable entity” (ship, drone, vehicle) is a node:

enum EntityType { Ship, Drone, Vehicle, RoverPlatform };

struct ProductionNode
{
    EntityType type;
    Seed seed;                       // deterministic procedural generation
    Vector3 bounds;                   // physical footprint
    vector<Module> modules;           // installed modules
    vector<ProductionNode*> children; // nested entities (e.g., drones on ship, vehicles in belly bay)
    float buildTime;                  // time to complete
    bool completed;
};
children allows recursive nesting: a ship node contains belly bay vehicle nodes, drone nodes, and potentially secondary rover nodes.

Each node’s seed locks layout, module placement, and hull configuration.

2️⃣ Integrated Belly Bay Vehicle / Fab System
struct BellyBay
{

    float maxVehicleSize;

6️⃣ Recursive Expansion & Seed-Locking
void ExpandProductionNode(ProductionNode& node)
{
    if (node.completed) return;

    for (auto& child : node.children)
    {
        // inherit host modules
        AssignModulesFromHost(*child, node);

        // procedural hull / node placement
        GenerateHullFromModules(*child);

        // recursive expansion if allowed (e.g., rover builds drones)
        ExpandProductionNode(*child);
    }

    node.completed = true;
}
Ships → belly bays → vehicles → modular drones

Rover platforms → configurable module nodes → small drones or resource nodes

All deterministic via seed lock

Hull silhouette governor enforces readability

Aesthetic entropy control ensures variation without chaos

Industrial cues emerge naturally: ramps, trusses, panels, exposed modules

void GenerateHullFromModules(ProductionNode& node)
{
    for (auto& module : node.modules)
    {
        SnapModuleToNode(module, node);           // procedural snapping
        ApplyIndustrialExtrusions(module);       // trusses, pipes, vents
        ApplySurroundedLowPolyStyle(module);     // flat faces, bold shapes
    }
}

1️⃣ Overall Pipeline
Ship Node
 ├─ Interior Systems
 │   ├─ Belly Bay (Rover/Grav Bike Fab)
 │   │   ├─ Rover Platforms (mobile mining/cargo/manufacturing)
 │   │   │   └─ Optional Modular Drones

 └─ Hull Generation

2️⃣ Core Data Structures
enum EntityType { Ship, BellyBay, RoverPlatform, Vehicle, Drone };

struct Module
{
    string name;
    Vector3 dimensions;
    ModuleType type;
    vector<Module> childModules; // recursive modules
};

struct ProductionNode
{
    EntityType type;
    Seed seed;
    Vector3 bounds;
    vector<Module> modules;
    vector<ProductionNode*> children;
    float buildTime;
    bool completed;
};
children allow nested procedural expansion

Modules define capabilities + visual style (industrial low-poly)

3️⃣ Recursive Generation Rules
void ExpandNode(ProductionNode& node)
{
    if (node.completed) return;

    // 1️⃣ Generate interior modules based on type
    GenerateModules(node);

    // 2️⃣ Generate child nodes where applicable
    for (auto& module : node.modules)
    {
        if (module.type == ModuleType::BellyBay)
        {
            ProductionNode* roverNode = GenerateVehicleNode(module, node.seed);
            node.children.push_back(roverNode);
        }
        if (module.type == ModuleType::DroneFab)
        {
            ProductionNode* droneNode = GenerateDroneNode(module, node.seed);
            node.children.push_back(droneNode);
        }
    }

    // 3️⃣ Assign procedural hull / industrial style
    GenerateHullFromModules(node);

    // 4️⃣ Recursively expand children
    for (auto& child : node.children)
        ExpandNode(*child);

    node.completed = true;
}
Ensures deterministic, recursive expansion

Industrial aesthetic emerges naturally via module snapping + hull generation

4️⃣ Build / Upgrade / Deployment Flow
struct BuildQueue
{
    ProductionNode* node;
    float timeRemaining;
    bool priority;
};

void ProcessBuildQueue(vector<BuildQueue>& queue)
{
    for (auto& job : queue)
    {
        job.timeRemaining -= deltaTime;

        if (job.timeRemaining <= 0)
        {
            job.node->completed = true;

            // Deploy to host if child of ship
            if (job.node->type == Vehicle || job.node->type == Drone)
                DockToParent(job.node);

            // Optionally queue next child builds
            for (auto& child : job.node->children)
                queue.push_back({child, child->buildTime, false});
        }
    }
}
Queued builds: ships → belly bay vehicles → drones → rover platforms

Upgrade interaction: player can select modules before or during build

Deployment happens automatically once build completes

5️⃣ Vehicle & Rover Platforms as Mobile Fabricators
void GenerateRoverPlatformNode(Module& module, Seed parentSeed)
{
    ProductionNode platform;
    platform.type = RoverPlatform;
    platform.seed = CombineSeed(parentSeed, module.name);
    platform.bounds = module.dimensions;

    // Assign modular nodes for mining / cargo / fab
    for (int i = 0; i < module.allowedSlots; i++)
        platform.children.push_back(GenerateDroneNodeForRover(platform.seed));

    return platform;
}
Each rover can carry modular drones

Can serve as mobile fab, cargo, or mining unit depending on installed modules

Seed-lock ensures deterministic procedural appearance

    }

{
    if (ramp.occupied) return false;
    if (rover.size > bay.maxVehicleSize) return false;

    // Optional: check if path is clear within bay
    return true;
}

void RoverEnterBay(BellyBay& bay, Rover& rover, RampNode& ramp)

    SnapRoverToRamp(rover, ramp);
    ramp.occupied = true;

    // Dock rover in bay slot after entering

struct GravBikeBay
{

    bool occupied;
    bool elevatorDeployed;
    float elevatorHeight;          // tracks descent to ground
    float speed;
    Vehicle* bike;
};
Elevator Deployment Logic:

void DeployGravBike(GravBikeBay& bay)
{
    if (!bay.occupied || bay.bike == nullptr) return;

    bay.elevatorDeployed = true;

    // Maglock disengagement occurs at ground level
    while (bay.elevatorHeight > 0)
    {
        bay.elevatorHeight -= bay.speed * deltaTime;
        UpdateElevatorPosition(bay.elevatorHeight);
    }

    MagLockDisengage(bay.bike);
    bay.occupied = false; // bike has left
}
Elevator acts as sub-room and interface hub

Provides player access to ship systems, crafting, storage during deployment

Deterministic placement ensures industrial low-poly aesthetic

            RoverEnterBay(bay, NextRover());

    // Grav bike deployment
    if (bay.gravBikeBay.occupied)
        DeployGravBike(bay.gravBikeBay);

    // Mobile rover platforms
    for (auto& slot : bay.vehicleSlots)
        if (slot.vehicle->type == RoverPlatform)
            ExpandNode(*slot.vehicle->node);

    // Player interface
    if (ElevatorUI.active)
        ElevatorUI.Open();
}
Recursively handles all vehicles, rover platforms, and sub-modules

Hull + module snapping ensures industrial Surrounded aesthetic

Deterministic and seed-locked

2️⃣ Core Data Structures
enum EntityType { Ship, BellyBay, Rover, GravBike, RoverPlatform, Drone };

struct Module
{
    string name;
    Vector3 dimensions;
    ModuleType type;
    vector<Module> childModules;  // nested functionality
};

struct ProductionNode
{
    EntityType type;
    Seed seed;
    Vector3 bounds;
    vector<Module> modules;
    vector<ProductionNode*> children; // recursive expansion
    float buildTime;
    bool completed;
};
children allow nested production nodes

Modules define functionality + procedural hull snapping cues

3️⃣ Recursive Expansion Logic
void ExpandNode(ProductionNode& node)
{
    if (node.completed) return;

    GenerateModules(node);                 // procedural interior + bay modules
    GenerateHullFromModules(node);         // snap hull to module layout

    for (auto& module : node.modules)
    {
        if (module.type == ModuleType::BellyBay)
        {
            ProductionNode* roverNode = GenerateVehicleNode(module, node.seed);
            node.children.push_back(roverNode);
        }
        if (module.type == ModuleType::DroneFab)
        {
            ProductionNode* droneNode = GenerateDroneNode(module, node.seed);
            node.children.push_back(droneNode);
        }
        if (module.type == ModuleType::RoverPlatform)
        {
            ProductionNode* mobileFabNode = GenerateRoverPlatformNode(module, node.seed);
            node.children.push_back(mobileFabNode);
        }
    }

    for (auto& child : node.children)
        ExpandNode(*child);

    node.completed = true;
}
Recursively expands all ships, bays, vehicles, platforms, drones

Hull snapping enforces readable industrial silhouettes

4️⃣ Build / Upgrade / Deployment Queue
struct BuildQueue
{
    ProductionNode* node;
    float timeRemaining;
    bool priority;
};

void ProcessBuildQueue(vector<BuildQueue>& queue)
{
    for (auto& job : queue)
    {
        job.timeRemaining -= deltaTime;

        if (job.timeRemaining <= 0)
        {
            job.node->completed = true;

            // Deploy to parent node if applicable
            if (job.node->type == Rover || job.node->type == GravBike || job.node->type == Drone)
                DockToParent(job.node);

            // Queue child nodes automatically
            for (auto& child : job.node->children)
                queue.push_back({child, child->buildTime, false});
        }
    }
}
Build queue handles ships → bays → vehicles → drones

Player upgrades and module swaps can insert or reorder queue items

Deployment occurs automatically when node completes

5️⃣ Vehicle & Grav Bike Integration
Rover / Grav Bike Entry:

void RoverEnterBay(BellyBay& bay, Rover& rover)
{
    for (auto& ramp : bay.ramps)
    {
        if (!ramp.occupied && rover.size <= bay.maxVehicleSize)
        {
            SnapRoverToRamp(rover, ramp);
            ramp.occupied = true;
            DockVehicle(bay, rover);
            return;
        }
    }
}

void DeployGravBike(GravBikeBay& bay)
{
    if (!bay.occupied || bay.bike == nullptr) return;

    bay.elevatorDeployed = true;
    while (bay.elevatorHeight > 0)
    {
        bay.elevatorHeight -= bay.speed * deltaTime;
        UpdateElevatorPosition(bay.elevatorHeight);
    }

    MagLockDisengage(bay.bike);
    bay.occupied = false;
}
Configurable ramp placement (front/back/side)

Grav bike elevator acts as sub-room + UI hub

Integrates procedural node snapping and hull modifications

6️⃣ Mobile Rover Platform as Mini-Fab
ProductionNode* GenerateRoverPlatformNode(Module& module, Seed parentSeed)
{
    ProductionNode* platform = new ProductionNode();
    platform->type = RoverPlatform;
    platform->seed = CombineSeed(parentSeed, module.name);
    platform->bounds = module.dimensions;

    // Optional drone children
    for (int i = 0; i < module.allowedSlots; i++)
        platform->children.push_back(GenerateDroneNodeForRover(platform->seed));

    return platform;
}
Modular role: mining, cargo, or on-demand manufacturing

Snap nodes dictate external hull silhouette and module placement

7️⃣ Procedural Hull Snapping + Aesthetic Enforcement
void GenerateHullFromModules(ProductionNode& node)
{
    for (auto& module : node.modules)
    {
        SnapModuleToHull(module);             // ensures proper node alignment
        ApplyIndustrialExtrusions(module);   // ramps, panels, trusses
        ApplyLowPolySurroundedStyle(module); // flat faces, bold silhouette
    }
}
Ensures all recursive expansions maintain industrial Surrounded low-poly readability

4️⃣ Integration With Ships & Vehicles
struct ProceduralNode
{
    EntityType type;              // Ship, BellyBay, Rover, Rig, Drone
    vector<Module> modules;
    vector<ProceduralNode*> children;
    Seed seed;
    float buildTime;
    bool completed;
};

void ExpandNode(ProceduralNode& node)
{
    GenerateModules(node);
    GenerateHullFromModules(node);   // ships, rovers, rigs all handled

    for (auto& module : node.modules)
    {
        if (module.type == ModuleType::DroneBay)
        {
            ProceduralNode* childDroneNode = GenerateDroneNode(module, node.seed);
            node.children.push_back(childDroneNode);
        }
    }

    for (auto& child : node.children)
        ExpandNode(*child);

    node.completed = true;
}
Player rigs now fully part of recursive system

Drone bays work identically to ship drone bays, preserving modularity and determinism

    FlattenFaces(module.mesh);
    ApplyBoldSilhouettes(module);
    AddIndustrialCues(module); // piping, vents, docking interfaces
}

void ExpandNode(ProceduralNode& node)
{
    if (node.completed) return;

    GenerateModules(node);               // interior / bay / rig modules
    SnapHullToModules(node);             // procedural hull snapping

    for (auto& module : node.modules)
    {
        if (module.type == ModuleType::DroneBay || module.type == ModuleType::MobileFab)
        {
            ProceduralNode* childNode = GenerateChildNode(module, node.seed);
            node.children.push_back(childNode);

    node.completed = true;

struct BuildQueue
{
    ProceduralNode* node;
    float timeRemaining;
    bool priority;
};

void ProcessBuildQueue(vector<BuildQueue>& queue)
{
    for (auto& job : queue)
    {
        job.timeRemaining -= deltaTime;

        if (job.timeRemaining <= 0)
        {
            job.node->completed = true;

            // Automatically queue children
            for (auto& child : job.node->children)
                queue.push_back({child, child->buildTime, false});

            // Deploy node if applicable
            DeployNode(job.node);
        }
    }
}

  │    │         └─ Optional Mini-Fab or Storage Modules
  │    └─ Drone Fabrication Bay (optional)

  ├─ Player Rig Node

Workflow Logic (Text Pseudo-Code)
// Main Expansion Pipeline
void ProceduralShipExpansion(ShipNode& ship)
{
    GenerateModules(ship);                 // interiors, hull, systems
    SnapHullToModules(ship);               // enforce Surrounded low-poly silhouette

    for (auto& module : ship.modules)
    {
        if (module.type == BellyBay)
        {
            ProceduralNode* bay = GenerateBellyBayNode(module, ship.seed);
            ship.children.push_back(bay);
        }

        if (module.type == PlayerRig)
        {
            ProceduralNode* rig = GeneratePlayerRigNode(module, ship.seed);
            ship.children.push_back(rig);
        }
    }

    for (auto& child : ship.children)
        ExpandNode(*child);                // recursively expand all child nodes
}

// Recursive Expansion for all nodes
void ExpandNode(ProceduralNode& node)
{
    GenerateModules(node);                 // module assignments
    SnapHullToModules(node);               // procedural hull snapping

    for (auto& module : node.modules)
    {
        if (module.type == DroneBay || module.type == MobileFab)
        {
            ProceduralNode* child = GenerateChildNode(module, node.seed);
            node.children.push_back(child);
        }
    }

    for (auto& child : node.children)
        ExpandNode(*child);

    node.completed = true;
}

// Build / Upgrade / Deployment Queue
void ProcessBuildQueue(vector<BuildQueue>& queue)
{
    for (auto& job : queue)
    {
        job.timeRemaining -= deltaTime;

        if (job.timeRemaining <= 0)
        {
            job.node->completed = true;
            DeployNode(job.node);

            for (auto& child : job.node->children)
                queue.push_back({child, child->buildTime, false});
        }
    }
}

// Player Interaction Integration
void OpenNodeInterface(ProceduralNode& node)
{
    if (node.type == GravBike || node.type == RoverPlatform)
        DisplayVehicleUI(node);

    if (node.type == PlayerRig)
        DisplayRigUI(node);

    if (node.type == Drone)
        DisplayDroneUI(node);
}

Ships → Belly Bay → Vehicles → Mobile Fab → Drones → Player Rig → Rig Drones

Procedural Hull Snapping

Hull shapes and silhouettes dynamically generated from interior modules and node placement

Industrial low-poly “Surrounded” aesthetic is emergent

Modular Upgrades Across All Systems

Ships, vehicles, mobile fabs, drones, player rigs, and rig drones all share modular node architecture

Dynamically handles all nodes, ensures deterministic timing and order

Player Interface Integration

Supports crafting, storage, system access, and drone deployment

Deterministic / Seed-Locked Generation

Same seed → same ship, vehicles, drones, rig configuration

Allows for replay, persistence, and player experimentation

2️⃣ Editor Contexts
Editor	Purpose	Modules	Snap Grid	Interactions
Ship Builder	Assemble hull + bays	Hull panels, belly bays, ramps, elevators, fab nodes	3D grid (X/Y/Z)	Drag, rotate, snap, preview exterior hull

3️⃣ Procedural Node + Grid System
struct SnapGrid
{
    Vector3 origin;
    Vector3 cellSize;
};

struct EditorModule
{
    string id;
    Vector3 size;          // bounds of module
    Vector3 position;      // snapped to grid
    Quaternion rotation;
    ModuleType type;
    SnapGrid* grid;        // reference to grid for snapping
    vector<EditorModule*> children;
};

Vector3 SnapToGrid(Vector3 rawPosition, SnapGrid* grid)
{
    Vector3 snapped;
    snapped.x = round(rawPosition.x / grid->cellSize.x) * grid->cellSize.x;
    snapped.y = round(rawPosition.y / grid->cellSize.y) * grid->cellSize.y;
    snapped.z = round(rawPosition.z / grid->cellSize.z) * grid->cellSize.z;
    return snapped + grid->origin;
}
Every module you drag snaps exactly to a 3D grid.

Child modules auto-align relative to parent node.

This applies to ships, bays, ramps, elevators, fabs, drones, rigs.

4️⃣ Suit & Rig System in the Editor
Power Armor Frame / Suit Rig acts like a mini-ship inside a grid.

Modules snap to skeleton points (shoulders, spine, limbs).

Player movement mode:

Mode	Effect on Systems	Movement
In Armor / Rig Active	Systems powered, module configuration active, drones docked or deployed	Restricted; powered mobility, boosts from modules
On Foot / Armor Removed	Only base suit modules active; drones remain docked	Full movement freedom; modules inactive
Full Rig Setup	All modules active, drone bays online	Heavily powered, slower, modular boosts active
Editor functionality:

Drag/drop armor plates & modules on rig skeleton

Snap drones to rig drone bays

Preview power connectivity and system status in real-time

Show movement limitations or boosts depending on current setup

5️⃣ Integration With Ship / Vehicle Builder
Player rigs snap inside ships:

Dynamic validation: prevents misaligned or overlapping modules

void PlaceModule(EditorModule& parent, EditorModule& child)
{
    child.position = SnapToGrid(child.position, parent.grid);
    parent.children.push_back(&child);
    
    if (child.type == ModuleType::DroneBay || child.type == ModuleType::MobileFab)
    {
        // recursively generate procedural nodes
        ProceduralNode node = GenerateProceduralNode(child);
        ExpandNode(node);
    }
    
    // Update hull / rig visuals immediately
    UpdateHullPreview(parent);
}
All drag & drop interactions automatically update procedural nodes, hull snapping, and system connections.

2️⃣ Procedural Flow Separation
void AssembleDroneInFab(ProceduralNode& fabNode)
{
    // Builds drone hull and physical modules
    ProceduralNode droneHull = GenerateDroneHull(fabNode.seed);
    SnapHullToModules(droneHull);   // Enforces industrial Surrounded aesthetic

    fabNode.children.push_back(&droneHull);
}

void ConfigureDroneInBay(ProceduralNode& droneBayNode, ProceduralNode& droneHull)
{
    // Assign roles and system modules
    droneHull.role = droneBayNode.selectedRole;   // Defense / Recon / Support
    droneHull.modules = droneBayNode.assignedModules;

    // Optional: display live configuration in Drone Bay UI
    UpdateDroneBayUI(droneHull);
}

No physical geometry changes — purely logical / UI layer

Rig Drone Bay

Similar pattern for up to 4 drones attached to player rig

Assign roles & modules

Hulls already built in Fab, only config applied

Workflow Logic (Pseudo-Code)
void PlaceModule(EditorModule& parent, EditorModule& child)
{
    // Snap child module to parent grid
    child.position = SnapToGrid(child.position, parent.grid);
    parent.children.push_back(&child);

    // Trigger procedural expansion for Fab or Drone Bay
    if (child.type == ModuleType::MobileFab)
    {
        ProceduralNode droneHull = AssembleDroneHull(child.seed);
        child.children.push_back(&droneHull);

        ProceduralNode vehicleHull = AssembleVehicleHull(child.seed);
        child.children.push_back(&vehicleHull);
    }

    if (child.type == ModuleType::DroneBay)
    {
        ConfigureDrone(child, child.linkedFabDrones);
    }

    if (child.type == ModuleType::PlayerRig)
    {
        for (int i = 0; i < 4; i++)
        {
            ProceduralNode rigDrone = LinkRigDrone(child.seed, i);
            child.children.push_back(&rigDrone);
        }
    }

    // Update hull / module visuals in real-time
    UpdateHullPreview(parent);
}

void ExpandNodeRecursive(ProceduralNode& node)
{
    // Recursively expand all child nodes
    for (auto& child : node.children)
    {
        SnapHullToModules(child);
        ExpandNodeRecursive(*child);
    }
}

1️⃣ Interior ↔ Exterior Principles
Aspect	Interior	Exterior Representation	Notes
Functional Zones	Belly bay, ramps, elevators, fab nodes, drone bays, crew quarters	Hull bulges, hatches, ramps, vents	Interior dictates where hull protrusions occur

Power & System Nodes	Sensors, reactors, life support, elevators	Hull plating, fins, antennae, vents	Readable silhouette for players, functional aesthetic cues
2️⃣ Procedural Exterior Generation Rules
Hull Follows Interior Volume

Every interior module contributes to convex hull and bounding volume.

Multi-deck, side or rear expansions automatically create bulges or extensions.

Hull snapping ensures low-poly polygons stay readable.

Functional Feature Mapping

Ramps → external sloped panels or doors

Elevator → reinforced airlock sections

Fab bays → industrial panels, vents, crane-like structures

Drone launch → small protrusions or vents

Rig docking → hull indentations or access clamps

Aesthetic Layering

Base hull: low-poly, simple geometric shapes

Modular accents: vents, panels, antennae, struts

Surface detailing constrained to Surrounded style → minimal triangles, readable silhouette, clean industrial feel

Semantic Hull Colors

Hull color / panel accents reflect interior function:

Belly Bay → reinforced metallic gray / yellow hazard panels

Fab / Drone areas → industrial orange / dark gray

Player Rig dock → neutral steel / tech blue
