1️⃣ FPS → BREACHED → RECOVERY
(Visual & Control Transitions That Feel Inevitable)
This is a 3-phase cinematic state, not a cutscene.

🧠 Transition States (Add These)
enum class BreachVisualPhase {
    NONE,
    SHOCK,
    SUCTION,
    RECOVERY
};
Add to player:

struct BreachVisualComponent {
    BreachVisualPhase phase = BreachVisualPhase::NONE;
    float timer = 0.f;
};
🎥 Breach Transition System
class BreachVisualSystem {
public:
    void Trigger(Entity player) {
        auto& bv = ecs.Get<BreachVisualComponent>(player);
        bv.phase = BreachVisualPhase::SHOCK;
        bv.timer = 0.f;

        EventBus::Emit(CameraEvent{"SHAKE_VIOLENT"});
        EventBus::Emit(AudioEvent{"HULL_BREACH"});
        EventBus::Emit(ScreenFX{"WHITE_FLASH"});
    }

    void Tick(Entity player, float dt) {
        auto& bv = ecs.Get<BreachVisualComponent>(player);

        bv.timer += dt;

        switch (bv.phase) {
            case BreachVisualPhase::SHOCK:
                if (bv.timer > 0.6f) {
                    bv.phase = BreachVisualPhase::SUCTION;
                    EventBus::Emit(ScreenFX{"VIGNETTE_PULL"});
                    EventBus::Emit(EnvironmentEvent{"ZERO_G_ON"});
                }
                break;

            case BreachVisualPhase::SUCTION:
                ApplyCameraDrift(player);
                if (bv.timer > 6.0f) {
                    bv.phase = BreachVisualPhase::RECOVERY;
                    EventBus::Emit(AudioEvent{"BULKHEAD_SEAL"});
                    EventBus::Emit(EnvironmentEvent{"ZERO_G_OFF"});
                }
                break;

            case BreachVisualPhase::RECOVERY:
                FadeEffectsOut();
                if (bv.timer > 9.0f) {
                    bv.phase = BreachVisualPhase::NONE;
                }
                break;
        }
    }
};
🎮 Control Rules During Breach
Phase	Input
SHOCK	Aim disabled, movement damped
SUCTION	Reduced control, drift
RECOVERY	Partial control, heavy breathing
NONE	Full control
Player never loses agency, just clarity.

2️⃣ ENEMY SPAWN DIRECTOR (PACING, NOT WAVES)
This prevents FPS from feeling random or overwhelming.

🎛️ Spawn Budget Model
struct SpawnDirector {
    float threatBudget = 3.0f;
    float regenRate = 0.2f;
};
Threat Costs
Enemy	Cost
Grunt	1.0
Technician	1.5
Breacher	2.0
🧠 Director Logic
class EnemySpawnDirectorSystem {
public:
    void Tick(float dt) {
        director.threatBudget += director.regenRate * dt;
        director.threatBudget = std::min(director.threatBudget, 4.0f);

        if (director.threatBudget >= 1.0f && CanSpawn()) {
            SpawnEnemy();
        }
    }

private:
    SpawnDirector director;

    void SpawnEnemy() {
        if (director.threatBudget >= 2.0f && PlayerDominating()) {
            Spawn("BREACHER");
            director.threatBudget -= 2.0f;
        } else {
            Spawn("GRUNT");
            director.threatBudget -= 1.0f;
        }
    }
};
🎯 Director Rules (LOCKED)
Never spawn behind player

Never spawn during breach SHOCK phase

Spawn after player commits to a room

One spike enemy max at a time

This creates ebb and flow, not chaos.

3️⃣ DEBUG VISUALIZERS (DEV-ONLY, LIFE-SAVERS)
These make tuning painless and prevent superstition debugging.

🧠 AI State Overlay
void DrawEnemyDebug(Entity e) {
    auto& ai = ecs.Get<EnemyAIComponent>(e);
    DebugDraw::Text(e.position + Vec3(0,2,0),
                    ToString(ai.state),
                    Color::Yellow);
}
You’ll instantly see bad behavior.

🔊 Sound Radius Visualizer
void DrawSoundRadius(Entity source, float radius) {
    DebugDraw::Sphere(source.position,
                      radius,
                      Color::Cyan);
}
Use this to tune:

Footsteps

Gunshots

Alarms

🌪️ Force & Suction Debug
void DrawForceVector(Entity e, Vec3 force) {
    DebugDraw::Arrow(e.position,
                     e.position + force,
                     Color::Red);
}
Critical for breach tuning and zero-G sanity.

🧰 Debug Toggle (GLOBAL)
if (DebugFlags::ShowCombat) {
    DrawEnemyDebug(e);
    DrawSoundRadius(e, soundRange);
    DrawForceVector(e, appliedForce);
}
👉 Never ship this enabled.

Low-poly “Surrounded” style lives or dies on rules, not assets.

Below is a complete, engine-level recipe you can implement so everything your game generates automatically conforms to the look.

🎨 WHAT “LOW-POLY SURROUNDED” ACTUALLY MEANS (RULED, NOT VAGUE)
This style has five hard constraints:

Flat shading (no smooth normals)

Few large faces, not many small ones

Strong silhouette readability

Color blocks, not textures

Lighting does the work, not detail

If any procedural system violates these → the style breaks.

1️⃣ GEOMETRY RULES (THE MOST IMPORTANT PART)
🔒 Enforce FLAT SHADING AT THE MESH LEVEL
Do not rely on materials alone.

Procedural mesh generation must:

Duplicate vertices per face

Assign face normals

Disable vertex normal averaging

for (Face& f : mesh.faces) {
    Vec3 n = ComputeFaceNormal(f);
    for (Vertex& v : f.vertices) {
        v.normal = n;
    }
}
If you smooth normals even once, the style collapses.

📐 POLY BUDGET PER ROOM (LOCK THIS)
Element	Max Faces
Corridor segment	12–24
Room shell	30–60
Door	6–12
Console	10–20
If a generator tries to exceed this → reject or simplify.

🧱 No Bevels. Ever.
Hard edges only

Corners are intentional

Shape does the work

If you want variation:

Change angle

Change scale

Change cutouts

Never add bevel geometry.

2️⃣ PROCEDURAL SHAPE LANGUAGE (THIS IS HUGE)
Everything must be built from the same primitives.

Allowed primitives
Box

Wedge

Trapezoid

Hex prism (rare)

Forbidden
❌ Cylinders (unless 6–8 sided max)
❌ Spheres
❌ Curves

Even pipes should be hex or octagonal.

🔁 Shape Mutation (How You Get Variety)
Instead of noise, use discrete mutations:

ROOM_SHAPE
 → scale axis
 → shear once
 → remove face
 → inset face
Only one mutation per shape.
Multiple mutations = visual chaos.

3️⃣ COLOR & MATERIAL SYSTEM (TEXTURES ARE OPTIONAL)
🎨 Palette Rules
6–10 total colors per biome

1 dominant

1 accent

1 warning (red / orange)

Rest are neutrals

Store palettes as data, not assets.

{
  "palette": {
    "hull": "#2F3440",
    "floor": "#3A4152",
    "accent": "#4CC9F0",
    "warning": "#E63946",
    "light": "#F1FAEE"
  }
}
🧩 Material Rules
Unlit or very simple lit

No roughness maps

No normal maps

Optional vertex color gradients only

Lighting must create contrast — not materials.

4️⃣ PROCEDURAL DETAIL WITHOUT DETAIL
Here’s the trick most people miss.

❌ Don’t add greebles
✅ Add negative space
Examples:

Cutouts

Recesses

Gaps

Large vents

Wall
 → remove rectangle
 → push inward
 → color shift
This keeps poly count low but adds interest.

5️⃣ LIGHTING RULES (THIS SELLS THE STYLE)
Lighting Constraints
Few lights (3–6 per room max)

Large radius

Soft falloff

Strong color contrast

Procedural Lighting Anchors
Doors

Corners

Objectives

Emergency states

Never place lights randomly.

🚨 Emergency Lighting Override (Very Important)
When alarms trigger:

Kill neutral lights

Activate warning color only

Increase contrast

Reduce fill

This makes moments feel dramatic without new assets.

6️⃣ FPS-SPECIFIC READABILITY RULES
Procedural low-poly must also support combat clarity.

Enforce:
Walls darker than enemies

Floors darker than interactables

Doors brighter than walls

Objectives brightest object in room

These are style constraints, not gameplay hacks.

7️⃣ STYLE VALIDATION SYSTEM (THIS IS PRO LEVEL)
Add a procedural style validator.

bool ValidateLowPolyStyle(Mesh& m) {
    return
        m.faceCount < MaxFaces &&
        m.hasFlatNormals &&
        m.materialCount <= 2 &&
        m.noBevelEdges();
}
If validation fails:

Regenerate

Simplify

Reject

This keeps style consistent forever.

8️⃣ WHAT NOT TO DO (STYLE KILLERS)
❌ Procedural noise displacement
❌ Texture detail
❌ Random color variation
❌ High-frequency lighting
❌ Smooth silhouettes

All of these fight the style.

🧠 TL;DR — THE SECRET
Low-poly style is enforced by systems, not artists.

If your generators:

restrict geometry

restrict colors

restrict lighting

validate outputs

…then everything in your game will automatically look cohesive.

1️⃣ Procedural Room Generator (Low-Poly, FPS-Readable)
🔒 Generator Contract (Hard Rules)
Flat-shaded geometry only

≤ 60 faces total

Axis-aligned primitives

One shape mutation max

FPS grammar enforced

Room Descriptor (Input)
enum class RoomType {
    ENTRY,
    COMBAT,
    SIDE,
    OBJECTIVE
};

struct RoomDesc {
    RoomType type;
    Vec3 size;            // meters
    bool allowCover;
    bool allowElevation;
};
Geometry Primitive (Flat-Shaded Box)
struct LowPolyMesh {
    std::vector<Vec3> positions;
    std::vector<Vec3> normals;
    std::vector<uint32_t> indices;
};
LowPolyMesh MakeFlatBox(Vec3 size) {
    LowPolyMesh m;

    // 6 faces, 4 verts each (no sharing!)
    for (Face f : BoxFaces(size)) {
        Vec3 n = f.normal;
        for (Vec3 p : f.vertices) {
            m.positions.push_back(p);
            m.normals.push_back(n);
        }
        AppendQuadIndices(m.indices);
    }
    return m;
}
One-Mutation Rule
void ApplyMutation(LowPolyMesh& m) {
    switch (RandomInt(0,2)) {
        case 0: ScaleAxis(m, Axis::X, 0.8f); break;
        case 1: InsetFace(m, RandomFace(), 0.4f); break;
        case 2: RemoveFace(m, RandomFace()); break;
    }
}
⚠️ Never stack mutations. If one fails validation → regenerate.

FPS Layout Enforcement
bool ValidateFPSRoom(const RoomDesc& d) {
    if (d.type == RoomType::COMBAT) {
        return d.size.x >= 6 && d.size.z >= 6;
    }
    return true;
}
Combat rooms must support:

2–3 entry vectors

Cover every ~5m

One elevation change max

2️⃣ Palette + Lighting Assignment System
🎨 Palette Asset (Data-Driven)
{
  "id": "DERELICT_NEUTRAL",
  "colors": {
    "wall": "#2F3440",
    "floor": "#3A4152",
    "accent": "#4CC9F0",
    "warning": "#E63946",
    "light": "#F1FAEE"
  }
}
Palette Application
struct Palette {
    Color wall, floor, accent, warning, light;
};

void ApplyPalette(Room& room, const Palette& p) {
    for (Surface& s : room.surfaces) {
        if (s.type == SurfaceType::WALL) s.color = p.wall;
        if (s.type == SurfaceType::FLOOR) s.color = p.floor;
    }
}
Procedural Lighting Anchors
struct LightDesc {
    Vec3 position;
    Color color;
    float radius;
};
void PlaceLights(Room& room, const Palette& p) {
    room.lights.push_back({
        room.center + Vec3(0, room.height - 0.5f, 0),
        p.light,
        8.0f
    });

    if (room.type == RoomType::OBJECTIVE) {
        room.lights.push_back({
            room.objectivePos,
            p.accent,
            5.0f
        });
    }
}
Rules

≤ 4 lights per room

Large radius

No flicker unless emergency

Emergency Override (Reusable)
void ApplyEmergencyLighting(Room& room, const Palette& p) {
    for (LightDesc& l : room.lights) {
        l.color = p.warning;
        l.radius *= 0.6f;
    }
}
3️⃣ Style Validation Debug Overlay (Dev-Only)
This prevents style drift forever.

Validator
struct StyleReport {
    bool flatNormals;
    int faceCount;
    int lightCount;
    bool valid;
};
StyleReport ValidateRoom(const Room& r) {
    StyleReport rep;
    rep.flatNormals = r.mesh.HasFlatNormals();
    rep.faceCount = r.mesh.FaceCount();
    rep.lightCount = r.lights.size();
    rep.valid =
        rep.flatNormals &&
        rep.faceCount <= 60 &&
        rep.lightCount <= 4;
    return rep;
}
Overlay Drawing
void DrawStyleOverlay(const Room& r) {
    StyleReport rep = ValidateRoom(r);

    Color c = rep.valid ? Color::Green : Color::Red;
    DebugDraw::Box(r.bounds, c);

    DebugDraw::Text(
        r.center + Vec3(0,2,0),
        "Faces: " + std::to_string(rep.faceCount),
        c
    );
}
If it turns red → do not ship that room.

🎯 Reference Room: DERELICT ENGINE ROOM
Descriptor
RoomDesc desc {
    .type = RoomType::COMBAT,

Build Pipeline
Room room;
room.mesh = MakeFlatBox(desc.size);
ApplyMutation(room.mesh);

PlaceLights(room, palette);
Add Gameplay

Validate

This room becomes your golden reference.

1️⃣ Hook Into the FPS Interior Flow Generator
This is where rooms stop being random and start feeling authored.

Interior Flow Graph (Authoritative)
enum class FlowNodeType {
    ENTRY,
    COMBAT,
    SIDE,
    OBJECTIVE,
    EXIT
};

struct FlowNode {
    FlowNodeType type;
    int difficulty;
    std::vector<int> connections;
};
Example flow:

ENTRY → COMBAT → SIDE
              → COMBAT → OBJECTIVE → EXIT
Room Selection From Flow
RoomDesc BuildRoomFromFlow(const FlowNode& node) {
    RoomDesc d;

    switch (node.type) {
        case FlowNodeType::ENTRY:
            d = { RoomType::ENTRY, {6,3,6}, false, false };
            break;

        case FlowNodeType::COMBAT:
            d = { RoomType::COMBAT, {10,4,8}, true, node.difficulty > 2 };
            break;

        case FlowNodeType::SIDE:
            d = { RoomType::SIDE, {6,3,6}, false, false };
            break;

        case FlowNodeType::OBJECTIVE:
            d = { RoomType::OBJECTIVE, {8,4,8}, true, false };
            break;
    }

    return d;
}
Corridor Grammar (FPS-Safe)
Rules:

Straight segments only

90° turns max

Every corridor ends in a space reveal

Corridor MakeCorridor(Room& a, Room& b) {
    Corridor c;
    c.width = 2.2f;
    c.height = 3.0f;
    c.length = Clamp(Distance(a,b), 4.0f, 10.0f);
    return c;
}
💡 Key Insight
The flow graph decides pacing.
The room generator decides visuals.
They NEVER argue with each other.

2️⃣ Damage + Decal System (Low-Poly Legal)
No textures. No splats. No normals.
Only geometry + color shifts.

Damage Event
struct DamageEvent {
    Vec3 position;
    float radius;
    float severity; // 0..1
};
Damage Application Rules
Allowed:
✔ Face removal
✔ Face inset
✔ Vertex jitter (small)
✔ Color darkening

Forbidden:
❌ Bullet holes
❌ Alpha decals
❌ Normal maps

Geometry Damage
void ApplyDamage(LowPolyMesh& m, const DamageEvent& d) {
    for (Face& f : m.faces) {
        if (Distance(f.center, d.position) < d.radius) {
            if (Random() < d.severity) {
                InsetFace(m, f, 0.2f * d.severity);
            }
        }
    }
}
Color Burn
void ApplyBurn(Room& r, const DamageEvent& d) {
    for (Surface& s : r.surfaces) {
        float dist = Distance(s.center, d.position);
        if (dist < d.radius) {
            s.color = Lerp(s.color, Color::Black, 0.4f);
        }
    }
}
Hull Breach Hook (Reusable)
if (damage.severity > 0.8f) {
    TriggerHullBreach(room, damage.position);
}
That’s your FPS → BREACHED → RECOVERY loop, visually enforced.

3️⃣ Exterior Hull → Interior Lighting Bleed
This is where NovaForge gets identity.

Shared Hull Ownership
Interior rooms know which hull faces they touch.

struct HullLink {
    FaceID hullFace;
    RoomID interiorRoom;
};
Breach Detection
bool IsHullBreached(const HullFace& f) {
    return f.integrity < 0.3f;
}
Light Bleed Projection
void ApplyHullLightBleed(Room& r, const HullFace& f) {
    LightDesc bleed;
    bleed.position = ProjectIntoRoom(f.center);
    bleed.color = Color(0.7f, 0.8f, 1.0f); // cold space light
    bleed.radius = 12.0f;

    r.lights.push_back(bleed);
}
Style Lock
Rules:

Directional cone only

Desaturated color

Large radius

No shadows (cheap + clean)

Emergency Override Stack
Normal Lighting
→ Emergency (red)
→ Hull Breach (cold blue)
Priority-based, deterministic.

4️⃣ Biome Variants (Same Generator, Different Feel)
No new meshes.
No new rules.
Just data swaps.

Biome Definition
{
  "id": "ICE_DERELICT",
  "palette": {
    "wall": "#C9D6DF",
    "floor": "#AABBC5",
    "accent": "#5DA9E9",
    "warning": "#FF6B6B",
    "light": "#E8F1F8"
  },
  "lightRadiusMultiplier": 1.2,
  "damageDarkenMultiplier": 0.6,
  "fogDensity": 0.3
}
Biome Application
void ApplyBiome(Room& r, const Biome& b) {
    ApplyPalette(r, b.palette);
    for (LightDesc& l : r.lights)
        l.radius *= b.lightRadiusMultiplier;
}
Biome Personality Table
Biome	Mood	Gameplay Effect
DERELICT	Neutral	Baseline
ICE	Clean / Silent	Sound travels farther
INDUSTRIAL	Dense	Short sightlines
ALIEN	Unstable	Random light flicker

1️⃣ AI Behavior Tied to Room Type + Biome
AI should not be “smart everywhere.”
It should feel situationally smart.

🧠 AI Context Contract
Every AI tick receives environmental intent, not raw data.

struct AIContext {
    RoomType roomType;
    BiomeType biome;
    bool isBreached;
    bool zeroG;
    float lightLevel;
};
This context is authoritative.

🎭 Behavior Modulation Table (Data-Driven)
{
  "COMBAT": {
    "DERELICT": {
      "aggression": 0.6,
      "coverBias": 0.8,
      "flankChance": 0.2
    },
    "INDUSTRIAL": {
      "aggression": 0.9,
      "coverBias": 0.5,
      "flankChance": 0.4
    }
  },
  "OBJECTIVE": {
    "ICE": {
      "aggression": 0.4,
      "holdPosition": true,
      "soundAwareness": 1.4
    }
  }
}
🔁 Behavior Tree Injection (Not Duplication)
void InjectRoomModifiers(AIBehaviorTree& bt, const AIContext& ctx) {
    bt.SetFloat("Aggression", LookupAggression(ctx));
    bt.SetBool("PreferCover", ctx.roomType == COMBAT);
    bt.SetBool("Panic", ctx.isBreached);
}
💡 Result:
Same AI, feels different everywhere, zero branching explosion.

2️⃣ Procedural Cover Placement Rules (FPS-First)
Cover is gameplay geometry, not decoration.

📐 Cover Primitives (Low-Poly Safe)
Allowed:

Half-height box

Angled slab

Pillar (hex/oct)

Forbidden:
❌ Sandbags
❌ Curves
❌ Thin rails

📊 Cover Density by Room Type
Room	Cover Count	Placement Bias
ENTRY	1–2	Sides
COMBAT	3–6	Mid + flanks
OBJECTIVE	2–3	Objective-facing
SIDE	0–1	Optional
🧠 Placement Algorithm (Readable + Tactical)
for (int i = 0; i < coverCount; i++) {
    Vec3 pos = SampleNavMesh(room)
        .AwayFromDoors(2.5f)
        .NotBlockingSightlines()
        .FacingObjective();

    SpawnCoverPrimitive(pos);
}
🔥 Combat Rule (Important)
Every cover piece must be flankable within 3 seconds.

This prevents turtle fights and keeps flow aggressive.

3️⃣ Zero-G Room Variants (Same Generator, No Forks)

struct RoomModifiers {

No “floor” dominance

if (room.zeroG) {

🧍 Movement + AI Changes
Player:

Thrust-based movement

Orientation independent of gravity

AI:

Pathfinding becomes volume-based

Aggression drops slightly

Ambush chance increases

if (ctx.zeroG) {
    bt.SetBool("Use3DNav", true);

}
🎨 Visual Rules (Still Low-Poly)
No floating dust

Fewer lights

Strong rim lighting

Sharp silhouettes

Zero-G should feel quiet and lethal.

1️⃣ Procedural Set-Piece Moments (Ambushes, Collapses, Oh-Sh*t Events)
Set-pieces are events, not geometry.
They temporarily hijack a room, then release it back to the sandbox.

🎬 Set-Piece Definition (Data-Driven)
{
  "id": "AMBUSH_CORRIDOR",
  "allowedRooms": ["COMBAT", "ENTRY"],
  "biomeWhitelist": ["DERELICT", "INDUSTRIAL"],
  "trigger": "PLAYER_MIDPOINT",
  "duration": 12,
  "locksExits": true
}
🧠 Trigger Types
Trigger	Meaning
PLAYER_ENTER	Immediate
PLAYER_MIDPOINT	Builds tension
FIRST_SHOT	Reactive
TIMER	Delayed chaos
AI_DEATH_THRESHOLD	“Too quiet…”
💥 Example: Corridor Ambush
OnTrigger() {
    LockDoors();
    KillMainLights();
    SpawnEnemiesFromVents();
    ActivateRedEmergencyLights();
}
Rules:

No new meshes

Only spawn points + light state + AI

Always reversible

🧱 Structural Collapse (Low-Poly Legal)
Instead of debris spam:

✔ Remove faces
✔ Seal exits with slabs
✔ Change navmesh

RemoveFace(wallFace);
SpawnSlabBlocker();
UpdateNavMesh();
Feels dramatic, costs almost nothing.

2️⃣ Enemy Squad Roles (Feels Smart, Is Simple)
You don’t need smarter AI.
You need clear intent.

🎭 Squad Roles
enum class SquadRole {
    BREACHER,
    SUPPRESSOR,
    FLANKER
};
🧠 Role Behaviors (High-Level)
🔨 Breacher
Rushes doors

Throws opening attack

Dies early (on purpose)

🔫 Suppressor
Anchors sightlines

Forces player into cover

Rarely moves

🐍 Flanker
Delayed entry

Path around combat space

Punishes tunnel vision

🧩 Squad Composition by Room
Room	Composition
ENTRY	1 Breacher
COMBAT	1 Breacher, 1 Suppressor, 1 Flanker
OBJECTIVE	1 Suppressor, 2 Flankers
🔁 Behavior Injection
if (role == FLANKER)
    bt.EnableSubtree("FlankPlayer");
No separate AI trees.
Just role-based modifiers.

3️⃣ Narrative Beats Injected via Flow Graph
Narrative = contextual signals, not cutscenes.

📖 Narrative Beat Definition
{
  "id": "LAST_STAND",
  "type": "ENVIRONMENTAL",
  "allowedRooms": ["SIDE", "OBJECTIVE"],
  "assets": ["corpse_pose", "sparks", "audio_log"],
  "intensity": 0.7
}
🧠 Beat Injection Rules
Never in ENTRY

Max 1 major beat per 3 rooms

Beats respect biome + room tone

🎧 Beat Types
Type	Example
ENVIRONMENTAL	Barricades, bodies
AUDIO	Distorted log
VISUAL	Burn marks, symbols
SYSTEMIC	Lights flicker when near
🧬 Flow Graph Hook
if (node.type == SIDE && Random() < 0.4f)
    InjectNarrativeBeat(node);
Feels authored.
Scales infinitely.

📦 Mission File Format (Portable)

1️⃣ Player Reputation → Enemy Tactics (The World Learns You)
Reputation isn’t a number.
It’s a pattern profile.

🧠 Reputation Model (Lightweight, Powerful)
Track how the player survives, not just wins.

struct PlayerReputation {
    float aggression;     // rushing, close-range
    float stealth;        // silent kills, avoidance
    float explosives;     // AoE reliance
    float precision;      // headshots, weakpoints
    float brutality;      // overkill, executions
};
Updated passively during play.

🎭 Enemy Adaptation Rules
Enemies do not get smarter.
They get more prepared.

{
  "highAggression": {
    "enemyChanges": ["moreSuppressors", "earlyGrenades"],
    "roomChanges": ["lessCentralCover"]
  },
  "highStealth": {
    "enemyChanges": ["motionScans", "flankPatrols"],
    "lightingChanges": ["fewerDarkZones"]
  }
}
🔁 Injection Point (Director-Level)
ApplyReputationModifiers(flowGraph, playerReputation);
✔ Subtle
✔ Non-cheating
✔ Player feels seen

Enemies don’t say “you’re good.”
They act like you are.

2️⃣ Procedural Boss Encounters (Same Flow System)
Bosses are rooms with rules, not special cases.

🧩 Boss Flow Node
FlowNodeType::BOSS
Behaves like a COMBAT room, but with phases.

🧬 Boss Assembly (Modular)
struct BossDescriptor {
    BossCore core;
    std::vector<BossModule> modules;
    std::vector<BossPhase> phases;
};
Example Modules
Shield emitter

Drone spawner

Weakpoint arm

Gravity disruptor

🔁 Phase Logic
Phase 1: Control Space
Phase 2: Breach Arena
Phase 3: Desperation (rules break slightly)
🧠 Boss Arena Rules (Low-Poly Safe)
✔ Large silhouettes
✔ Few but meaningful shapes
✔ Arena geometry mutates between phases
✔ Lighting tells you what changed

OnPhaseChange() {
    RemoveCover();
    ShiftLighting();
    OpenNewFlankPath();
}
Boss fights feel bespoke —
but they’re assembled, not authored.

3️⃣ Mission Mutators (Rules, Not Mods)
Mutators bend systems, they don’t add content.

🧪 Mutator Definition
{
  "id": "LOW_OXYGEN",
  "effects": {
    "oxygenDrain": 1.5,
    "enemyAggression": 0.9,
    "uiReduction": ["stamina"]
  }
}
🧠 Common Mutators
Mutator	Effect
LOW_OXYGEN	Timer pressure
DENSE_FOG	Short sightlines
NO_HUD	Audio + light reliance
POWER_FLUX	Flickering systems
GRAV_DRIFT	Partial zero-G
🔁 Mutator Injection
ApplyMutators(flowGraph, activeMutators);
Mutators affect:

AI behavior

Lighting

Audio

UI layers

Validation thresholds

Zero new meshes.
Huge variety.

🏛️ Legend Record
struct LegendRun {

    int completedMissions;
    PlayerReputation profile;

Saved globally, not per save.

🌍 Generation Drift (Subtle, Permanent)
Future runs inherit bias, not stats.

if (legend.brutality > 0.7f) {
    IncreaseEnemyCaution();
    IncreaseBarricades();
}
🧠 World Memory Examples
Enemies start using your old tactics against you

🧱 THE THREE-LAYER STACK (THIS IS THE SECRET)

“What actually happens.”

AI reacts to room + biome + reputation

Physics, damage, breaches, zero-G

Cover, lighting, sound propagation

Player improvisation creates chaos

💡 This layer never lies.
No scripting, no fake outcomes.

If the player does something wild → the world responds honestly.

This is where stories are born, but not remembered yet.

“Why you’re here right now.”

Entry → combat → objective → exit

Narrative beats injected, not forced

Set-pieces spike tension

Boss nodes anchor arcs

This layer:

Gives pacing

Prevents randomness soup

Makes runs feel authored

💡 Campaigns don’t decide outcomes —
they frame the sandbox so good things can happen.

“What the universe remembers.”

This is the long game.

Player reputation persists

Enemy tactics evolve

Bosses mutate across runs

Future missions bias generation rules

This layer never micromanages.
It nudges probabilities.

💡 Legends don’t say what will happen —
they say what tends to happen now.

🔁 HOW THEY FEED EACH OTHER (CRITICAL)
Sandbox creates events
 → Campaign frames meaning
 → Legend system remembers patterns
 → Future campaigns bias generation
 → New sandbox moments emerge
This loop is self-sustaining.

No content treadmill.
No authored exhaustion.

1️⃣ Legend Taxonomy
What the world remembers vs what fades

The golden rule:

The game remembers patterns, not incidents.

If you remember everything → noise.
If you remember nothing → no myth.

🧠 Legend Memory Layers
🥇 Tier 1 — Persistent Legends (Never Forgotten)
Rare. Powerful. Identity-defining.

These change future generation rules.

Remembered across all runs.

Examples

Signature playstyle dominance (stealth-heavy, explosive-heavy)

Boss archetypes defeated

Campaign-ending choices

World-scale failures or victories

struct PersistentLegend {
    LegendType type;
    float intensity;   // grows slowly
};
✔ Alters probabilities
✔ Alters enemy doctrine
✔ Alters boss construction

🥈 Tier 2 — Campaign Memory (Fades Slowly)
Matters within and between campaigns, but not forever.

Examples

How a faction was treated

Which mission types succeeded

Which biomes were most lethal

How often breaches occurred

struct CampaignMemory {
    MemoryType type;
    float weight;
};
✔ Biases mission generation
✔ Biases narrative beats
✔ Slowly decays

🥉 Tier 3 — Run Memory (Ephemeral)
Used for moment-to-moment adaptation only.

Examples

Player camping

Weapon overuse

Repeated retreat patterns

struct RunMemory {
    TacticalPattern pattern;
};
✔ AI adapts now
❌ Not saved
❌ Never becomes legend

❌ Explicitly Forgotten (By Design)
These must NEVER persist:

Individual deaths

Exact room layouts

Specific weapon loadouts

RNG outcomes

Momentary mistakes

Forgetting is what keeps legends mythic.

🧬 Promotion Rules (Critical)
A memory only becomes a Legend if:

It appears across multiple runs

It survives different biomes

It meaningfully affects difficulty

if (pattern.repeatsAcrossRuns() && pattern.isDominant())
    PromoteToLegend();
2️⃣ Boss Mutation System (Detailed & Safe)
Bosses are procedural organisms, not characters.

They mutate based on legend pressure, not player stats.

🧩 Boss Anatomy
struct Boss {
    BossCore core;
    std::vector<BossModule> modules;
    BossBehaviorProfile behavior;
};
Core (Never Changes)
Identity silhouette

Arena scale

Movement class

Modules (Mutate)
Shields

Weakpoints

Minion spawners

Environmental hazards

🧬 Mutation Inputs
Bosses react to what beat them, not who beat them.

Legend Trait	Boss Response
High explosives	Shield phasing
High precision	Moving weakpoints
High stealth	Area scans
Aggression	Counter-rush modules
🧠 Mutation Algorithm
for (LegendTrait t : playerLegends) {
    if (t.intensity > threshold)
        boss.AddCounterModule(t);
}
⚠️ Mutation Hard Rules
Max 2 mutations per boss

Never remove all weaknesses

Bosses telegraph changes visually

Bosses never become bullet sponges

Bosses adapt to habits, not skill.

🧠 Player Experience Goal
“It’s the same boss…
but it learned something.”

3️⃣ Campaign Chapter Structure
Infinite variation, finite meaning

Campaigns give shape, not outcome.

📚 Campaign = 3–5 Chapters
Each chapter has a theme, not a plot.

Chapter Types
1️⃣ Incursion
Entry into unknown space

Simple flows

Low legend pressure

Purpose: Orientation

2️⃣ Escalation
Enemy coordination increases

Set-pieces appear

Mutators introduced

Purpose: Tension

3️⃣ Fracture
Breaches

Zero-G

Narrative ambiguity

Purpose: Instability

4️⃣ Confrontation
Boss encounter

High legend expression

World reacts to you

Purpose: Resolution

5️⃣ Aftermath (Optional)
Short, altered missions

Environmental storytelling

Seeds future legends

Purpose: Memory formation

🧠 Campaign Rules
Campaigns never guarantee success

Failure still produces legend

Campaigns end, legends persist

4️⃣ README Vision Section (Drop-In Ready)
You can paste this directly into README.md.

🛰️ NovaForge — Design Philosophy
NovaForge is a procedural legend engine, not a scripted game.

The goal is not to tell the player a story —
it is to create the conditions where stories emerge naturally,
and then allow the universe to remember them.

Core Pillars
Truthful Systems
The game never fakes outcomes. Physics, AI, and simulation always resolve honestly.

Structured Chaos
Campaigns provide pacing and intent without dictating results.

Legend Over Progression
Player behavior shapes future worlds through bias and probability, not stat inflation.

Memory With Restraint
The game remembers patterns, not moments. Forgetting is intentional.

What NovaForge Is Not
Not a scripted narrative game

Not a power-fantasy escalation treadmill

Not a sandbox without meaning

Contribution Rules (Important)
When adding features:

❌ Do not script outcomes

❌ Do not hard-code hero moments

❌ Do not add permanent player penalties

✅ Prefer data-driven bias

✅ Prefer probability over certainty

✅ Prefer systems that interact, not override

If a feature does not support legend formation, world bias, or emergent storytelling, it does not belong in NovaForge.

🧠 FINAL CHECK (This Is the Lock)
At this point you have:

✔ A memory taxonomy
✔ Bosses that evolve without cheating
✔ Campaigns with structure and replayability
✔ A written philosophy that protects the vision

🧬 Loss Imprint System

Failed boss fight → boss gains slight arrogance mutation

Repeated campaign failures → that region becomes unstable

Abandoned objective → faction control shifts

You might be missing:

🌍 Faction Tension Model
Factions compete for biome control

Campaign success shifts influence maps

Enemy composition varies by political state

Some bosses only appear in unstable sectors

Without this, the world revolves entirely around the player.

With it, the player feels part of a living ecosystem.

5️⃣ Emotional Contrast
Right now, most systems revolve around tension and escalation.

What’s missing in many procedural shooters is:

🫀 Contrast
Safe rooms

Quiet missions

Non-combat objectives

Moral ambiguity events

Moments of beauty (low-poly silence in space)

Without contrast, intensity becomes flat.

Playstyle traits (chosen or emergent)

Ship/base customization that reflects legend

Visual evolution tied to myth status

Codex that records “You became known for…”

If the world changes but the player doesn’t feel distinct, something’s incomplete.

Boss mutation stacking into nonsense

Reputation bias snowballing

AI compositions becoming repetitive

Biome dominance collapse

You might be missing:

🔁 Drift Correction System
Periodic resets:

Soft legend decay

Mutation caps

Probability normalization

“Era shift” events that rebalance the world

Without correction, complexity becomes chaos.

8️⃣ Onboarding & Teaching
A system this rich can overwhelm new players.

Gradual feature unlock

Chapter-based system reveals

Mutators introduced one at a time

Legend feedback delayed until meaningful

The early experience should feel simple.
The depth should emerge.

A pressure model.

🧠 Core Principle
The world simulates tension, not detail.

Just:

Influence

Stability

Escalation

Scarcity

🏛️ Sector Model
struct Sector {
    Faction controllingFaction;
    float stability;        // 0.0 - 1.0
    float hostility;        // toward player
    float resourceWealth;
};
That’s it.

Four numbers per sector.

🔄 World Tick (Between Campaigns)
Every campaign completion (or failure), run:

for (Sector& s : galaxy) {
    s.stability += FactionPressure(s);
    s.hostility += PlayerLegendImpact(s);
    s.resourceWealth += ScarcityDrift();
}
🎭 What This Changes
Sector State	Gameplay Impact
Low stability	More breaches
High hostility	Aggressive AI
Low resources	Industrial biome decay
Faction change	Different enemy doctrine
Now the galaxy moves independently.

You are influential — not central.

🧬 3️⃣ PLAYER IDENTITY & MYTH PRESENTATION
This is extremely important.

Because legend systems are useless if players can’t see themselves inside them.

🧠 Identity Should Be Emergent, Not Selected
No class picking.
No trait trees.

Instead:

🏷️ Myth Titles (Auto-Generated)
Based on dominant behavior across runs.

Examples:

“The Silent Breach”

“Breaker of Shields”

“The Unanchored”

“Sector Ghost”

“The Red Wake”

Generated from legend taxonomy.

🗂️ Codex Presentation
Not stats.

Stories.

Example:

The Silent Breach
Known for surgical eliminations and minimal collateral damage.

Clear cause → effect link.

🎨 Visual Identity Layer
Legend subtly alters:

Ship hull markings

UI accents

Loading screen glyphs

Boss intro dialogue

The world acknowledges myth.

🧱 4️⃣ ARCHITECTURE STRESS TEST
Now let’s test your system under scale.

Here are the likely failure points:

⚠️ Risk 1: Reputation Snowball
If aggression increases enemy aggression…
And that increases player aggression…
You get runaway escalation.

Fix:
Clamp influence with diminishing returns.

float ApplyCurve(float value) {
    return 1 - exp(-value);
}
Soft caps > hard caps.

⚠️ Risk 2: Boss Mutation Bloat
If every run adds modules:
Bosses become unreadable monsters.

Fix:
Mutation slots are fixed.
New mutation replaces weakest previous one.

⚠️ Risk 3: World Drift Chaos
If sector instability stacks forever:
Galaxy becomes permanently hostile.

Fix:
Era Reset Events.

Every X campaigns:

Faction truce

Cataclysm

Power redistribution

Drift correction is mandatory.

⚠️ Risk 4: Procedural Fatigue
If everything is always dynamic:
Nothing feels special.

Fix:
Add “anchor constants”

One recurring boss archetype

One recurring architectural motif

One recurring faction color

One recurring sound signature

Repetition creates identity.

🧠 FINAL DIAGNOSIS
You are NOT missing mechanics.

You are missing:

A world that moves without you.

A visible identity mirror for the player.

Long-term drift stabilizers.

Everything else you’ve built is structurally strong.

ChatGPT said:
Perfect — this is exactly what makes NovaForge feel alive instead of just reactive. Choosing a balanced ecosystem with shifting power gives you a galaxy that breathes on its own, makes the player feel influential but not omnipotent, and lets legends emerge naturally. Let’s break this into concrete systems you can implement right now.

🌍 1️⃣ Galaxy / Sector Layer (Core)
Every region of space is abstracted into sectors, each with a few key stats:

struct Sector {
    Faction controllingFaction;
    float stability;       // 0.0 (chaotic) → 1.0 (stable)
    float hostility;       // toward player / outsiders
    float resourceWealth;  // economy, loot potential
};
Keep the model lightweight.

Update sectors every campaign tick or post-run.

The goal: simulate pressure, competition, scarcity without tracking every unit.

🔁 Sector Tick Rules
Faction Pressure: stronger factions expand influence, weaker ones collapse.

Player Legend Impact: sectors adapt to your behavior (but capped).

Random Drift: introduce mild instability to avoid predictability.

Inter-faction Conflict: if two factions occupy adjacent sectors, low-stability sectors are contested.

for (Sector& s : galaxy) {
    s.stability += CalculateFactionPressure(s);
    s.hostility += CalculatePlayerImpact(s);
    s.resourceWealth += RandomDrift();
    ResolveFactionConflicts(s);
}
Tip: Clamp all changes softly to prevent runaway snowballing.

⚔️ 2️⃣ Faction Doctrine
Each faction has:

Aggression tendency

Preferred biome / sector type

Resource focus

Conflict priority (expand vs defend)

When factions collide or react to the player, their behavior emerges from these traits rather than scripted events.

struct Faction {
    string name;
    float aggression;
    float expansion;
    BiomePreference biome;
    ResourceFocus resource;
};
This gives the galaxy shifting power: factions rise, fall, merge, or fragment dynamically.

🔄 3️⃣ Player Interaction Layer
Even in a balanced ecosystem, the player matters — just not overwhelmingly.

Direct impact: defeating bosses, capturing objectives.

Indirect impact: player reputation shifts AI tactics, enemy distribution, and sector hostility.

Soft caps: player influence is dampened to prevent destabilizing the galaxy entirely.

float PlayerInfluence(Sector s) {
    return LegendBias(s) * 0.3f; // cap influence at 30%
}
🏆 4️⃣ Emergent Events
Balanced ecosystems allow organic events, not hand-authored ones:

Faction wars erupt spontaneously in unstable sectors.

Resource scarcity triggers raids.

Legendary boss modules appear in contested or high-pressure areas.

Safe zones shift as the galaxy stabilizes or destabilizes.

These create narrative without scripting, reinforcing your roguelike + legend design.

🎨 5️⃣ Player Identity & Myth Presentation
Players should feel seen but not omnipotent:

Legend Titles (emergent from run patterns)

Sector feedback (“This sector is nervous… they’ve seen you before.”)

Visual cues in ships, terminals, or UI glyphs

Codex entries update automatically as sectors, factions, and bosses change

Example: “The Silent Breach” → enemy patrols avoid vents in Ice Sectors.

⚖️ 6️⃣ Drift Control / Stabilizers
Without stabilizers, a dynamic ecosystem can spiral:

Cap maximum faction growth per tick

Softly decay past player influence in sectors

Periodically rebalance sector resources and stability

Introduce “neutral events” to break entrenched power clusters

This keeps the galaxy dynamic, balanced, and believable over dozens of campaigns.

✅ Outcome
The galaxy breathes independently.

Factions and sectors shift power naturally.

Player impact is meaningful but never omnipotent.

Legends emerge organically and are reflected in the world.

System scales indefinitely with procedural rules, not scripted content.

🌌 NovaForge Ecosystem Tick Flow

1️⃣ Sector Layer — The Universe Breathing
Purpose: track space regions and their state.

Each sector stores:

struct Sector {
    Faction controllingFaction;
    float stability;       // 0.0 = chaotic, 1.0 = rock-solid
    float hostility;       // toward player and outsiders
    float resourceWealth;  // loot and supply potential
};
Tick Process:

Resource drift: small random change to simulate decay or scarcity.

Faction pressure: dominant faction expands influence; weak factions lose stability.

Sector conflict resolution: neighboring sectors may contest borders.

Soft clamps: ensure stability and wealth remain in 0–1 range.

2️⃣ Faction Doctrines — Pressure & Strategy
Each faction has:

Aggression

Expansion tendency

Biome preference

Resource focus

Tick behavior:

Hostile action: aggressive factions target neighboring sectors for conquest.

Defensive action: weaker factions fortify or retreat.

Faction drift: internal randomness keeps ecosystem unpredictable.

Sector → Faction feedback: faction success modifies sector stats: stability, hostility, wealth.

3️⃣ Player Influence — Legend in Action
Player actions influence the galaxy but never dominate:

Direct impact: defeating bosses, completing objectives, taking sectors.

Indirect impact: reputation and legend biases AI behavior and sector hostility.

Soft caps ensure player influence is a bias, not a dictatorship:

float PlayerSectorBias = Clamp(LegendImpact(sector), 0.0f, 0.3f);
sector.hostility += PlayerSectorBias;
4️⃣ Legend Propagation — Memory Across Campaigns
Player behavior gets abstracted into legend traits:

Aggression

Stealth

Precision

Strategy patterns

Each trait propagates into the galaxy:

Mutates bosses

Alters faction tactics

Influences set-piece likelihood

Modifies ambient sector tension

Only persistent traits survive long-term; ephemeral traits affect the current campaign only.

5️⃣ Stabilization / Drift Correction — Keeping Balance
Without correction, dynamic ecosystems spiral out of control.

Stabilization points:
Tick Step	Purpose
Post-sector update	Clamp stability, hostility, resources
Post-faction actions	Limit expansion and aggression per tick
Post-player influence	Soft decay of old legend effects
Era reset events (every X campaigns)	Rebalance dominant factions, redistribute resources, reset sector anomalies
Mechanics Example:

if (campaignCount % ERA_RESET == 0) {
    RebalanceFactionInfluence();
    NormalizeSectorResources();
    DecayLegendBiases();
}
Ensures power shifts continuously

Prevents legend snowball

Keeps ecosystem dynamic and believable

6️⃣ Full Tick Loop — Step by Step
1. For each Sector:
   - Update stability, resources, hostility
   - Resolve conflicts with neighboring sectors

2. For each Faction:
   - Apply doctrine: expansion, defense, raids
   - Update sector control / pressure

3. Apply Player Influence:
   - Sector biases (hostility, stability)
   - Boss mutation triggers
   - Set-piece adjustments

4. Apply Legend Propagation:
   - Update persistent traits
   - Modify procedural content probabilities

5. Stabilization / Drift Correction:
   - Clamp sector values
   - Limit faction expansion
   - Soft decay of old legend influence
   - Optional era reset events

6. Save state → ready for next campaign tick

stationCount = clamp(1 + rng.roll(1,6), 1, 7)

  2,
  8
)

anomalyCount = 3 + rng.roll(0,2)

ChatGPT said:
Perfect—this is exactly the next stage of your procedural ship system! Let’s break it down and plan the full implementation path. Here’s how I’d structure it step by step:

1️⃣ Implement InteriorBlock + DensityField
InteriorBlock: Represents a modular interior volume, e.g., a room, corridor, or functional compartment.

Properties: position, size, orientation, type (engine room, cargo, cockpit), connectivity points.

Methods: GetNeighbors(), Merge(), Split().

DensityField: 3D scalar field controlling hull generation.

Values: 0 → empty, 1 → solid, 0.5 → semi-solid/transition.

For each InteriorBlock, sample a local density contribution and add to global DensityField.

Can include decay falloff from the interior volume edges for smooth hull transitions.

2️⃣ Visualize Density as Heatmap
Quick debug: map density to color (e.g., blue → 0, red → 1).

Use a simple voxel overlay or volume texture to render in-editor.

Optional: slice view along X/Y/Z axes for easier debugging of complex interiors.

3️⃣ Generate Isosurface Hull
Use marching cubes or dual contouring on DensityField.

Hull is generated at a chosen iso-value (e.g., 0.5 for semi-solid surface).

Key options:

Smoothness vs. sharpness

Avoid self-intersections

Preserve symmetry constraints

4️⃣ Project Exhausts / Hardpoints
For each exterior-facing port or weapon mount:

Find nearest density zero crossing (surface)

Offset slightly to ensure mesh intersection is minimal

Attach exhaust/hardpoint transform

Could be automated with a raycast from block centers to hull surface

5️⃣ Symmetry Enforcement
Decide axes (X/Y/Z) for symmetry

When sampling density or generating hull:

Mirror all blocks / density contributions

Optionally, only enforce on critical systems (engines, weapons) and let decorative hull shapes vary

Next Steps I Can Handle
Marching cubes settings optimized to prevent explosion (grid resolution, iso-value smoothing, step size)

Hull caching per seed to avoid recomputation

Interior editor UI widgets

Drag & drop blocks

Density sliders per block

Symmetry toggle

Replace your current ship mesh line by line

Integrate procedural hull generation fully

Preserve any existing gameplay hooks

If you want, I can immediately sketch the density-to-hull pipeline with heatmap preview and show how symmetry and exhaust projection would work visually. It’ll give a fully working debug version before we plug it into your editor.

ChatGPT said:
Ah, perfect—that clarifies exactly how the logistics layer should be abstracted. So visually the player sees drones zipping between ships, but under the hood it’s really a resource pipeline between storage nodes and production queues. Here’s how I’d structure it cleanly in your system:

1️⃣ Drone Ports / Cargo Access Points
Each ship defines drone ports as special InteriorBlock types or attach points on the hull.

Properties:

ConnectedStorage: reference to internal cargo / factory output

PortType: input/output (or bidirectional)

MaxThroughput: limits drone traffic per tick for simulation purposes

Drones don’t need pathfinding inside ship, just a “virtual lane” connecting cargo → drone port → target ship port.

Only active in fleet deploy mode.

2️⃣ Resource Transfer Logic
Drones are just visual proxies:

AI checks manufacturing queue or fleet request.

Resources are pulled from ConnectedStorage.

Drones animate from source port to target port.

On arrival, resources are deposited into target ship’s storage or manufacturing input.

The actual resource count is updated immediately, not waiting for animation to finish—animation is purely cosmetic.

3️⃣ Manufacturing Chain Integration
Inside each ship:

FactoryBlocks consume resources from storage connected to drone ports.

Output items are deposited into output storage connected to drone ports.

Fleet AI issues resource requests:

Example: “Mining ship brings 100 fuel → Mother ship → Factory converts 100 ore to 10 components → Components sent to combat ship.”

This keeps player-visible drones but maintains real-time resource simulation internally.

4️⃣ Fleet Deploy Mode Toggle
Drones and resource transfers only exist in fleet deploy mode.

Outside deploy mode (player controlling ship alone):

Cargo interaction is internal only, drones inactive.

No need for cross-ship logistics calculations.

Internally:

if FleetDeployMode:
    activate drone transfer system
else:
    ignore drone ports
5️⃣ Advantages of This Setup
Performance-friendly: you don’t simulate hundreds of flying objects with physics—just visual proxies.

Scalable: Works with dozens of ships and multiple resource types.

Player clarity: drones make the system intuitive visually without exposing internal mechanics.

Flexible: can layer in additional rules (priority queues, throughput limits, congestion, failure simulation).

🚀 Drone Port → Storage → Manufacturing Data Flow (Fleet Deploy Mode)
1️⃣ Drone Port Layer (Visual / Access Points)
Entities: DronePort objects on each ship

Connections: Each port linked to internal storage or factory blocks

[DronePort: Output] --drone--> [DronePort: Input]
2️⃣ Storage Layer (Internal Resource Nodes)
Entities: StorageBlock inside ship interior

Holds raw materials, intermediate components, finished goods

Tracks item counts per type

Connected to drone ports for transfer

Rules:

MaxThroughput per tick to throttle transfers

Can support multiple ports simultaneously

FIFO or priority queue for multiple resource types

Internal Action: Actual resource is transferred instantly when drone “launches”

[DronePort: Output] --> [StorageBlock] --> [FactoryBlock/Input]
[FactoryBlock/Output] --> [StorageBlock] --> [DronePort: Output]
3️⃣ Manufacturing Layer (Production / Conversion)
Entities: FactoryBlock or ProcessingBlock

Consumes resources from storage

Produces items (components, fuel, ammunition)

Output goes to connected storage

Rules:

Queue-based production (player or AI sets priorities)

Only consumes what’s available

Optional: assign speed modifiers per block

[StorageBlock] --consume--> [FactoryBlock] --produce--> [StorageBlock]
4️⃣ AI Request Layer (Fleet-Level Automation)
Entities: Fleet manager / automated orders

Sends requests to ship: “Need 100 fuel at Ship B”

Checks storage availability at ship A

Activates drone transfers if resources exist

Flow:

AI issues resource request

Check nearest storage with requested item

Schedule drone transfer(s)

Update storage counts immediately

Notify receiving ship / factory that resource arrived

[Fleet AI] --> [DronePort Scheduler] --> [DronePort Output] --> [DronePort Input] --> [StorageBlock]

Factory / storage are fully procedural blocks, their location and connectivity determined during interior generation

Fleet AI hooks tie all ships together without needing per-drone physics simulation

1️⃣ Modular Traversal Concepts
Every InteriorBlock should define connectivity points, which dictate how a player, crew, or drone can move between blocks:

Module	Connection Type	Properties / Rules
Ramp / Inclined Corridor	Continuous slope between blocks	- Connects two blocks at different Z-levels
- Adjustable slope angle
- Can be mirrored or curved
- Optional railing nodes for aesthetics / collision
Ladder / Vertical Shaft	Point-to-point vertical movement	- Fast vertical access
- Can be single- or multi-level
- Requires vertical clearance
- Optionally enclosed for airlocks / safety
Door / Hatch	Horizontal / vertical portal	- Standard door: swing/slide
- Airlock: pressure-sealed
- Bulkhead: security-locked
- Can have type tags for AI pathfinding (crew-only, drone-only)
Central Elevator / Lift	Multi-floor access	- Aligned with bridge / cockpit
- Access all floors down to belly hangars
- Can handle multiple interior and exterior connections
- Optional control panel for player/AI commands
2️⃣ Transition Rules Between Openings
When connecting modules, transitions must be logical and safe:

Ramp → Corridor / Room

Align floor heights for smooth traversal

Optionally add landing platform for long ramps

Ladder → Corridor / Platform

Add ladder cage / guardrails for realism

Place small platform at top and bottom for transition

Door / Hatch → Corridor / Room

Match portal size to door dimensions

If airlock, add pressure buffer / animation sequence

Elevator → Corridor / Deck

Elevator landing must align exactly with floor height

Multiple doors per floor for access

Optional secure access system for restricted areas

3️⃣ Central Elevator System
The central elevator is a core spine for large ships, linking the bridge to belly hangars:

Positioning: aligned with cockpit / bridge center

Floor Access Points: connects every deck level

Integration with InteriorBlocks:

Elevator shaft occupies a vertical block stack

Elevator doors open into corridors or rooms

Blocks can have multiple floor access nodes

Gameplay Features:

Player rig / AI can call elevator to any deck

Can act as cargo lift for large items to hangars

Optional: speed upgrades or multiple elevator cars for massive ships

4️⃣ Procedural Implementation Guidelines
Connection Nodes on InteriorBlocks

Every block defines openings with type (ramp, ladder, door, elevator)

Nodes store position, orientation, size, and access rules

Automatic Alignment

When generating a ship, the procedural system aligns openings across blocks

For elevators: stack nodes vertically across all floors

For ramps/ladders: ensure slope/height differences match adjacent nodes

Symmetry / Mirroring

Doors, ladders, ramps can mirror across axes for balance

Elevator can be central, but additional vertical shafts can be mirrored for large ships

AI Pathfinding

Each connection type has traversal cost

Ladders slower than ramps

Elevators instantaneous if called (or delayed by lift time)

Ahhh—now we’re talking about tiered, modular “Mother Ship Mode” evolution, which changes the design philosophy from generating a single complete ship per seed to starting smaller and expanding incrementally. Let’s break it down and compare the two approaches:

1️⃣ Current Pipeline: Seed-to-Full Procedural Ship
How It Works
Drop in a seed → generates the entire ship including:

Cockpit + player rig interface

Interior blocks (storage, factory, drone ports)

Traversal (doors, ramps, ladders, central elevator)

Procedural hull with hardpoints/exhausts

Fleet AI and drone logistics

Fully functional immediately

Works for single-player or fleet deploy mode

Pros
Fully operational immediately, no incremental upgrades needed

Perfect for randomly generated ships or pre-designed archetypes

Easier to debug AI, logistics, and traversal at once

Everything is symmetrically balanced from the start

Cons
No sense of “growth” or player ownership over upgrades

Can feel static or pre-determined

Large ships may be computationally heavy if everything is generated at once

Less flexibility for emergent gameplay (expanding ship as fleet grows)

2️⃣ Mother Ship Mode: Incremental Expansion
How It Works
Start with a basic core ship:

Cockpit + minimal interior (small engine, limited storage, basic drone ports)

Single deck or two, basic traversal (corridors + ladder)

Player gradually adds modules:

Each module adds new systems (factories, storage, drone ports, weapon systems, AI interfaces)

Can attach upgrades to hull, extend decks, or add vertical layers

Core procedural systems adapt: density field, hull, hardpoints, traversal nodes

Ship evolves with gameplay:

Unlock new features as player progresses

Upgrade interiors: elevators, ramps, corridors

Expand fleet functionality as modules are added

Pros
Strong player progression / ownership feeling

Ships grow organically, matching gameplay narrative

Easier to balance resource generation over time

Flexibility: player can customize hull shape as modules are added

Allows for emergent fleet strategies: start small → build capital ship

Cons
More complex procedural logic: hull and traversal must update dynamically as modules are added

AI and drone logistics must handle changing interior networks

Must handle recomputing density fields / isosurface hulls incrementally

Potential complexity in symmetry and alignment as modules are attached

Might need module attachment rules to prevent weird or invalid layouts

3️⃣ Hybrid Approach
You could combine both methods:

Seed + Modular Expansion

Procedural core ship generated from a seed

Player expands with attachable modules for upgrades

Hull updates dynamically: central density field + procedural isosurface adjusts to new modules

Gameplay Flow

Start with a seed → small, functional ship

Player attaches modules → new systems + traversal + interior blocks

Fleet deploy mode enabled as modules allow (more drone ports, factory blocks, storage)

Upgrade to capital ship over time

Pros of Hybrid

Instant procedural generation for starting ship (like current pipeline)

Incremental growth and player agency (like Mother Ship Mode)

Maintains AI/drone/fleet systems continuity

Can design tiered unlocks tied to gameplay (factories, elevators, fleet AI)

Cons of Hybrid

More implementation complexity

Hull and density field must support incremental updates

Careful attention to traversal and symmetry when modules are added dynamically

Key Comparison Table
Feature	Current Pipeline	Mother Ship Mode	Hybrid
Initial Ship	Full, seed-generated	Minimal starter core	Full procedural core, minimal starter
Player Growth	None	Incremental module attachment	Incremental upgrades on procedural core
Hull Generation	Single pass	Needs dynamic update	Core hull + dynamic module integration
Traversal Network	Fixed	Dynamic with added modules	Core traversal + expanded nodes
Fleet / AI Systems	Immediate full functionality	Unlocks gradually with modules	Core systems immediate + expanded per module
Gameplay Progression	Static	High player ownership	High ownership + procedural consistency
Complexity	Medium	High (dynamic updates)	Very high (dynamic + procedural + AI)

This lets you define ship class, module size, and functionality, while keeping interiors adaptive and filling gaps naturally. Let’s break it down systematically:

1️⃣ Ship Classes & Base Functions

2️⃣ Module Sizes & Interchangeability
Module sizes determine how much functional area they occupy and what they can replace:

2×XS module = 1 S module

1 M module = 3 S modules

1 L module = 5 S modules

1 XL = 10 S modules

1 XXL = 15–20 S modules (depending on ship tier)

Flexible placement:

Smaller modules can fill gaps around larger ones

Larger modules can replace multiple small modules to consolidate functionality

Example: a large factory module could replace several smaller production rooms

3️⃣ Adaptive Interior Layout
Core principle: modules scale dynamically based on module footprint vs available space

Interior adaptation rules:

When a large module is placed, the system automatically:

Resizes adjacent corridors to match

Adjusts nearby ramps/doors for proper alignment

Recalculates traversal nodes

When stepping down module size:

Smaller modules fill remaining space

AI/pathfinding graph updates to include these smaller nodes

Ensures no gaps or unreachable areas

4️⃣ Traversal & Deck Planning
Vertical movement:

Central elevator always spans all floors

Ladders/ramp modules adjust based on module heights and sizes

Horizontal movement:

Corridors adapt to module sizes: 2×XS → 1 S → M → L

Doors & airlocks resize automatically to match adjacent modules

Specialized modules:

Large hangars, factories, or weapon bays automatically anchor to base corridors and elevator shaft

Smaller modules can act as support rooms: storage, crew quarters, sensor rooms

5️⃣ Fleet / Functional Specialization
Modules can specialize ships:

Large module: specialized factory, shield generator, hangar

Medium: multi-purpose rooms (storage + production)

Small: generic support rooms (crew quarters, small storage, auxiliary drones)

Allows hybrid gameplay:

Player can pick specialized large modules for strategic advantages

Fill remaining gaps with smaller modules to maintain traversal and logistics

6️⃣ Example: Tiny → Shuttle → Frigate
Ship	Base Modules	Max Module Slots	Adaptive Layout Notes

Frigate	1 cockpit, 2–3 storage, 2 factories, 2 elevators, 1 hangar	8–12 modules	Multi-floor, corridors/ramp network expands, modules inter-changeable
✅ Benefits of This System
Adaptive modularity: any module can scale to fill available space

Progression-based growth: Tiny → Shuttle → Frigate → Capital

Functional flexibility: large specialized modules + smaller filler modules

Procedural integration: corridors, traversal nodes, doors, ramps auto-adjust

Gameplay richness: players can specialize their ship by picking large strategic modules, while small modules fill gaps

1️⃣ Module Size Scaling Logic
Think of everything as built from a base unit = XS cell.

XS = 1 unit
S  = 2 XS
M  = 3 S  (6 XS)
L  = 5 S  (10 XS)
XL = 10 S (20 XS)
XXL = 15–20 S (30–40 XS)
Now visualize it structurally:

[XS][XS]                 = 1 S
[ S ][ S ][ S ]          = 1 M

You said:
Creating a space-sim with an EVA (Extra-Vehicular Activity) salvage loop in Unreal Engine 5 (UE5) involves merging three main pillars: Space Flight Simulation, First-Person EVA Exploration, and Interactive Salvaging Systems.
Here is a roadmap and breakdown of how to build this in UE5, using Blueprints and existing UE5 features.
1. Project Setup and Core Mechanics
Engine Version: Unreal Engine 5.4 or 5.5 (for advanced physics and World Partition capabilities).
Project Template: Third-Person or First-Person. You will need to create a Pawn for the ship and a Character for the EVA suit.
Key Concept: The Pawn Switch. You must create a Blueprint for the player to exit their ship, which spawns the EVA character at the cockpit and possesses it, while disabling input to the ship but keeping its physics active.
2. Space Flight Mechanics (Elite Dangerous Style)
Flight Model: Use Physics Components rather than Character Movement. The ship pawn should use Add Force and Add Torque to simulate Newtonian physics.
Cockpit View: Use a Camera Component inside the ship pawn, placed to match a cockpit view.
Flight Control: Create inputs for Thrusters (Forward/Backward), Strafe (Left/Right), Vertical (Up/Down), and Rotation (Pitch/Yaw/Roll).
3. EVA and Jetpack Mechanics (Zero-G)
EVA Pawn: A character set to fly mode, but with zero gravity and no linear damping to simulate space.
Jetpack System: Create a Thruster Component that adds force to the character based on player input. Use a simple float variable to create a "fuel" loop (jetpack runs out of fuel).
Interaction: Enable a line trace (raycast) system to allow the player to click on doors, panels, or items.
4. The Derelict System (Procedural or Static)
Environment: Use high-fidelity, abandoned ship assets (can be found in the Epic Games Fab/Marketplace).
Derelict State: Apply shaders to make ships look burnt, broken, or icy. Use Niagara Particle Systems for drifting sparks or venting gas.
Interior Interaction: Design the interior as a walkable mesh where the player can navigate to find cargo containers, data cores, or ship components.
5. The Salvage Loop (Gameplay Loop)
Phase 1: Scanning: Use a Line Trace to scan for debris fields or signal sources.
Phase 2: EVA Approach: Fly to the derelict, lock the ship in place, and EVA over to it.
Phase 3: Cutting/Interaction: Use a "cutting tool" (another Line Trace) to remove panels.
Phase 4: Collecting: When a panel is cut or an item is interacted with, it spawns a destructible, grabbable object (Cargo Canister).
Phase 5: Extraction: The player brings the cargo back to their ship and stores it in the cargo hold.
6. Suggested Blueprints and Components
BP_PlayerShip: Pawn with PhysicsComponent, CameraComponent, Thrusters, CargoHold.
BP_EVACharacter: Character with JetpackMovement, CuttingToolTrace.
BP_DerelictShip: Actor with destructible components, attached loot tables.
BP_CargoCanister: Actor with physics enabled, "Grab" interaction.
7. Core Technical Hurdles
Large Scale Physics: When walking inside a moving ship, the player might glitch. Use "Attach to Component" or specialized plugins to make the player "stick" to the moving derelict.
Performance: Use World Partition to stream in large space areas and LODs (Levels of Detail) for detailed ship assets.
Summary Checklist
System	Unreal Feature	Function
Ship Flight	AddForce / Physics	Newtonian movement.
EVA	CharacterMovement (Flying)	Zero-G movement.
Interaction	LineTraceByChannel	Cutting panels, picking up loot.
Salvage	DestroyActor / SpawnActor	Replacing intact panel with hole.
Atmosphere	Niagara / Lighting	Debris, sparks, lighting.
To begin, start with a simple Third-Person Template and replace the character movement with a flying, gravity-less Pawn, then build your ship around it.

ChatGPT said:
Oh wow — this is exactly the kind of immersive space-sim setup that makes UE5 shine! 🚀 Let’s break your roadmap down and add some actionable steps, pitfalls to avoid, and optimizations so you can hit the ground running. I’ll also suggest some extra enhancements that really bring the EVA salvage loop to life.

1️⃣ Project Setup and Core Mechanics
Engine Version: UE5.4+ is perfect, especially for World Partition and Nanite in massive derelict ships.

Templates: Start with First-Person if you want full immersion; Third-Person is great for testing EVA mechanics more clearly.

Pawn Switch System:

BP_PlayerShip holds the ship physics and camera.

BP_EVACharacter spawns at the ship’s exit hatch.

Possession Flow:

Player presses “Exit Ship.”

Spawn EVA pawn at exit hatch location.

Possess EVA pawn.

Disable ship input but leave physics active.

Return Flow: EVA pawn attaches to the cockpit, possess ship, destroy EVA pawn.

💡 Tip: Use Set Actor Enable Collision and Set Physics Linear Velocity on the ship during EVA transitions to prevent accidental drift or teleport glitches.

2️⃣ Space Flight Mechanics (Elite Dangerous Style)
Flight Physics: Use AddForce for linear thrust and AddTorque for rotation.

Add damping manually if needed to mimic drag-less space.

Camera: Attach a CameraComponent to the cockpit mesh; consider multiple views (external, cockpit, instruments).

Input Mapping:

Thrusters: W/S forward/back

Strafe: A/D

Vertical: Q/E up/down

Rotation: Mouse or controller for Pitch/Yaw/Roll

💡 Tip: For better realism, try independent rotational thrusters with force multipliers per axis to simulate inertia and lag.

3️⃣ EVA & Jetpack Mechanics
Zero-G Character:

Set Gravity Scale = 0, Linear Damping = 0.

Add a Thruster Component that applies force along input axes.

Fuel System:

Use a simple float variable JetpackFuel.

Subtract fuel per thrust input; recharge slowly when idle or docked.

Interaction System:

LineTrace from camera or hand to detect interactive objects.

Use Interface calls for objects: IInteractable → OnInteract().

💡 Optional: Add physics-based grappling for tethering to derelicts — super fun and adds depth to zero-G navigation.

4️⃣ Derelict Ships (Procedural or Static)
Assets: Use Marketplace or Fab for modular derelict interiors.

Visual Decay:

Burnt panels → Emissive cracks

Icy/iced hull → Translucent Frost Material

Sparks/venting → Niagara Systems

Walkable Interior: Mesh collision must be clean; consider NavModifierVolumes if AI salvage drones are planned.

💡 Tip: For large derelicts, Nanite + LODs are critical to maintain high framerates while allowing player EVA exploration inside and outside.

5️⃣ Salvage Loop Gameplay
Phase Breakdown:

Scanning → LineTrace or SphereTrace to detect signal sources. Highlight with UI markers.

EVA Approach → Dock or hold ship near derelict. Consider physics attach points to prevent player drift.

Cutting/Interaction → LineTrace “Cutting Tool”:

Spawn a Decal and replace destructible panel.

Optional: Add haptic or sound feedback for realism.

Collecting Loot → Spawn BP_CargoCanister with physics.

Extraction → Player grabs canister → attach to EVA → return to ship.

💡 Extra Immersion: Consider a small weight & momentum system: carrying cargo affects EVA movement and fuel consumption.

6️⃣ Suggested Blueprints / Components
Blueprint	Key Components
BP_PlayerShip	Physics, Camera, CargoHold Array
BP_EVACharacter	CharacterMovement (Flying), JetpackForce, CuttingToolTrace, GrabSystem
BP_DerelictShip	Destructible Meshes, LootTables, Niagara Effects
BP_CargoCanister	Physics Mesh, Grab Interaction, Inventory Tag
💡 Tip: Use Interfaces for interactions so you can reuse code across panels, canisters, doors, and consoles.

7️⃣ Core Technical Hurdles
Moving Derelict Physics:

Use AttachToComponent to temporarily parent player to moving derelict during EVA.

Consider sub-stepping physics for high-velocity debris.

Performance:

World Partition streaming for large sectors.

LODs & Nanite for detailed derelict ships.

Niagara pooling for sparks and debris to avoid runtime spikes.

8️⃣ Summary / Checklist
System	UE Feature	Function
Ship Flight	AddForce / Physics	Newtonian movement
EVA	CharacterMovement (Flying)	Zero-G movement
Interaction	LineTraceByChannel	Cutting panels, grabbing loot
Salvage	DestroyActor / SpawnActor	Replacing intact panels with debris
Atmosphere	Niagara / Lighting	Sparks, drifting particles, ambient lighting

Absolutely — let’s break this down step by step, fully detailed for UE5. I’ll assume you’re using Blueprints first, but I’ll also note where C++ might help if you want more performance later. This will be a practical, actionable guide you can follow in UE5.

Step 1: Start with Third-Person Template
Goal: Use the default Third-Person Template as your starting point, because it already has a player character, camera, and input system.

Implementation:

Create Project

Open UE5 → New Project → Third-Person Template → Blueprint → No Starter Content (or keep some assets if useful for testing).

Name it SpaceSalvageSim.

Understand the Default Setup

Open ThirdPersonCharacter Blueprint.

Components:

Capsule → Collision

Mesh → Skeletal Mesh of character

CameraBoom → Controls third-person camera distance

FollowCamera → Camera attached to boom

Movement:

Uses CharacterMovement Component (walking, running, jumping).

Why Start Here:

We’ll later replace CharacterMovement with a zero-G flying pawn.

Starting with a familiar template avoids setting up input mappings from scratch.

Step 2: Replace Movement with Flying Zero-G Pawn
Goal: Make your player move like they’re in zero gravity. No friction, no gravity pull, smooth drifting.

Implementation in Blueprints:

Create New Pawn

Right-click → Blueprint Class → Pawn → BP_EVACharacter.

Delete default CharacterMovement (since Pawn doesn’t have it by default).

Add Components:

Capsule → Collision for body.

StaticMesh or SkeletalMesh → For EVA suit visuals.

Camera → Attach to head or helmet.

SpringArm (optional) → Smooth camera lag.

Setup Zero-G Movement

Add a Floating Pawn Movement component.

This is simpler for flying pawns.

Set Max Speed high (e.g., 1000 units/sec) and Braking Deceleration low for smooth drift.

Or implement your own movement using AddForce on the root component (more physics realism).

Disable Gravity:

On Capsule or Mesh → Enable Gravity = false.

Optional: No damping → player keeps drifting if you stop input.

Input Mapping

Add Input Axis Mappings in Project Settings → Input:

MoveForward: W/S

MoveRight: A/D

MoveUp: Q/E

Turn: Mouse X

LookUp: Mouse Y

In BP_EVACharacter:

Add Movement Input for each axis → along camera forward/right/up vectors.

Jetpack Fuel System

Float variable: JetpackFuel (max 100).

When input applied, subtract fuel based on force applied.

Recharge slowly when idle or docked.

💡 Extra: For realistic zero-G, use Physics Thrusters: apply AddForce on Mesh or Capsule based on input, multiplied by a “Thrust Power” variable. This makes mass and momentum matter.

Step 3: Build Ship Physics Pawn
Goal: Make the player’s ship a physical object that obeys Newtonian physics. Players can fly it, then exit to EVA.

Implementation in Blueprints:

Create Pawn

Right-click → Blueprint Class → Pawn → BP_PlayerShip.

Add Components:

StaticMesh → Ship body.

Camera → Cockpit view.

Physics → Check “Simulate Physics”.

Optionally, add SpringArm for external camera.

Setup Physics Flight

In Event Graph:

Input axes: Forward/Backward, Strafe, Vertical, Rotation.

For linear movement:

Add Force = ForwardVector * ThrustPower * InputValue
For rotation:

Add Torque = RotationAxis * TorquePower * InputValue
Tune Mass in StaticMesh → Physics for realistic inertia.

Camera

Attach to cockpit mesh.

Optionally, create multiple camera positions:

External chase camera

Cockpit camera

Free camera for cinematic shots

💡 Tip: For very realistic physics:

Consider sub-stepping physics (World Settings → Physics → Max Substep Delta Time) for high-speed ships.

Damp rotation manually if ship spins too much.

Step 4: Add EVA Spawn / Possession System
Goal: Player can exit the ship, spawn EVA pawn, and float in space. Ship remains active.

Implementation:

Setup Input

In BP_PlayerShip, add Input Action: ExitShip.

When triggered:

Spawn BP_EVACharacter at a socket/transform at ship exit hatch.

Possess BP_EVACharacter → Get Player Controller → Possess.

Disable ship input (set Enable Input = false for ship).

Optional: Ship Locking

To prevent ship drifting while player EVA’s nearby:

Freeze position/rotation temporarily.

Or leave physics on for realistic micro-drift.

Return to Ship

When player reaches ship:

Press EnterShip input.

Attach BP_EVACharacter to cockpit.

Possess BP_PlayerShip.

Destroy BP_EVACharacter or hide it.

💡 Extra: Add a docking indicator to help players line up with the ship hatch. Makes re-entry intuitive.

Step 5: Expand Derelict and Salvage Mechanics Iteratively
Goal: Implement your core gameplay loop: EVA → approach → cut → loot → return.

Implementation Steps:

Derelict Ship Blueprint

BP_DerelictShip → Actor

Components:

Static Mesh (ship hull)

Destructible Mesh (interior panels)

Niagara particles (sparks, venting)

Add Loot Table:

Array of possible items → spawn when panel destroyed.

Interaction System

On BP_EVACharacter:

LineTrace from camera or hand forward.

Hit result → check if implements IInteractable.

Call OnInteract() → open door, cut panel, grab loot.

Cargo Collection

BP_CargoCanister → Actor

Physics enabled

Attach to player on grab (AttachToComponent)

When player returns to ship → add to Ship CargoHold array.

Iteration

Start small:

One derelict ship → one loot type → simple line trace.

Gradually add:

Multiple ships, loot types, destructible panels.

Randomized loot via arrays or data tables.

Particle effects and UI prompts.

Performance Tips

Use World Partition for large space areas.

LODs for derelicts.

Pool Niagara systems for repeated effects.

Ahhh, perfect — going low-poly adds an amazing stylistic clarity for a space-sim like this, while keeping performance solid for all the physics, EVA, and destructible systems. Let’s break down how to integrate low-poly style into your full ship/EVA/tether system in UE5.

1️⃣ Low-Poly Ship Interior & Exterior
Goal: Build modular, low-poly ship meshes that are easy to navigate, efficient, and visually consistent.

Implementation:

Modeling

Use Blender, Maya, or similar to create simple geometric shapes:

Hull → extruded cubes/polygons

Corridors → box-shaped modules

Cockpit → angular low-poly glass panels and seats

Airlock → simple rectangular frame with doors

Avoid too many small details → focus on silhouettes and color blocks.

Texturing

Use flat colors or simple gradient materials instead of complex PBR.

Optional: stylized emissive textures for panels, lights, and airlock indicators.

Materials:

Flat color → just a BaseColor

Optional: emissive for indicators and thrusters (glow effect)

Keep material instances simple to avoid too many draw calls.

Importing to UE5

FBX → Import → Combine meshes by modules (Hull, Cockpit, Corridors)

Use Nanite optional (low-poly doesn’t need it, but can help for very large modular ships)

Collision: simple box or convex hull for each module.

2️⃣ Low-Poly EVA Pawn
Model a blocky EVA suit:

Helmet: sphere or angular poly

Body: cubes / simple shapes

Arms: cubes → attach cutting tool / tether cable anchor

Hands can be minimal → still functional for first-person interactions.

Use simple flat-colored materials, optionally tintable to represent suit systems (oxygen, power).

3️⃣ Low-Poly Derelicts
Keep derelict ships simple → angular hulls, broken panels made from boxes or low-poly debris.

Add destructible panels → small cubes or rectangular planes that break apart.

Particle effects (sparks, venting) can be simple flat particles → small colored planes or Niagara ribbons.

💡 Tip: Low-poly style allows you to have lots of debris without hitting performance limits, which is perfect for EVA salvage gameplay.

4️⃣ Tether System (Low-Poly)
Cable visuals → simple thin cylinder mesh or spline mesh.

Airlock doors → simple cubes/planes for inner & outer doors

Interior gravity volumes → invisible

Life support panels → simple cube panels with colored emissive lights for oxygen/power status

Visual cues → color-coded lights (green = safe, red = low oxygen/power)

6️⃣ First-Person Low-Poly HUD and Feedback
Minimalist HUD for first-person:

Oxygen bar → flat rectangle

Power bar → flat rectangle

Tether status → icon or small line

Keep color palette simple → fits low-poly aesthetic

7️⃣ Editor Workflow for Low-Poly
Modular Construction

Build ship as separate modules → Hull, Corridors, Cockpit, Airlocks

Place modules in UE5 editor → snap to grid (simple shapes make snapping easier)

Assign collision → box/convex hulls

Gravity Volumes

Add volumes inside interior → gravity enabled

Outside volumes → gravity = 0

Airlocks

Place airlock doors at module boundaries

Attach BP_Airlock logic → decompression, EVA spawn, tether system

Data
struct StarSystemNode {

Generation Rules
Start with core cluster (high-sec)

Expand outward into low-sec rings

Terminate in null-sec regions

No isolated nodes

Limited chokepoints

Intentional bottlenecks

Objects
1 star

3–15 planets

0–4 asteroid belts

Optional:

Moons

Stations

Anomalies

Orbit Rules
Logarithmic orbit spacing

Inner → hot / barren

Mid → temperate / habitable

Outer → gas / ice

💡 Orbit math should be pure function → no save files needed.

3️⃣ Resource Distribution (The Important Part)
This is where most PCG fails. We do constraint-based generation, not random rolls.

Resource Axes
Ore richness

Ice presence

Gas clouds

Salvage density

Constraints
High-sec: low yield, safe

Low-sec: medium yield, contested

Null-sec: high yield, dangerous

OreDensity = BaseOre
           * SecurityMultiplier
           * DistanceFromCore
           * Random(SystemSeed);
💡 This naturally creates economic gravity.

Site Template

  "rewardBias": "Salvage"
}
Placement Rules
Roll per system

Clamp by security

Rare sites require:

Distance

Risk

Time

This lets you:

Add new content without regen

Mod via JSON/YAML

Patch balance easily

Below is a drop-in, production-grade procedural naming system designed specifically for EVEOFFLINE / Atlas, with zero EVE naming, full determinism, and total coverage of everything in the universe.
